## Task 5.2 - 实现 JwtUtils：基于配置生成/解析 JWT（含非法与过期识别）
- Date: 2026-05-02
- Status: Done
- Implemented: Added java-jwt as the selected JWT library for common-auth. Added JwtProperties with minimall.auth.jwt configuration fields for secret and expireSeconds. Added JwtUtils for generating HMAC256 JWTs with userId/username claims and parsing raw or Bearer-prefixed tokens back into UserContext. Invalid, tampered, expired, missing, and malformed-claims tokens are mapped to BusinessException with ErrorCode.UNAUTHORIZED.
- Changed files: common-auth/pom.xml; common-auth/src/main/java/com/minimall/common/auth/config/JwtProperties.java; common-auth/src/main/java/com/minimall/common/auth/jwt/JwtUtils.java; common-auth/src/test/java/com/minimall/common/auth/config/JwtPropertiesTest.java; common-auth/src/test/java/com/minimall/common/auth/jwt/JwtUtilsTest.java; .taskmaster/tasks/tasks.json; docs/dev-log.md
- Commands run: task-master next; task-master show 5.2; task-master set-status --id=5.2 --status=in-progress; local Maven cache check for JWT libraries; mvn -pl common-auth -am test; mvn clean package -DskipTests; task-master set-status --id=5.2 --status=done
- Test result: Initial mvn -pl common-auth -am test exposed a Bearer-without-token edge case; after fixing normalizeToken, mvn -pl common-auth -am test succeeded with common-core 12 tests passing and common-auth 17 tests passing. mvn clean package -DskipTests succeeded for the full 10-module reactor.
- Issues: No JWT library was found in the local Maven cache before implementation, so Maven resolved java-jwt during the test run. WSL still prints a NAT/localhost warning after commands, but commands completed successfully.
- Next: Task 5.3 - 实现 UserContextFilter + 自动装配：读取 JWT/透传头并在请求结束清理.

## Task 5.3 - 实现 UserContextFilter + 自动装配：读取 JWT/透传头并在请求结束清理
- Date: 2026-05-02
- Status: Done
- Implemented: Added UserContextFilter as a reusable OncePerRequestFilter for common-auth. The filter prioritizes X-User-Id/X-Username propagation headers, falls back to Authorization Bearer JWT parsing when available, writes UserContextHolder for downstream code, returns 401 with ApiResponse on invalid auth input, and clears ThreadLocal state in finally. Added CommonAuthAutoConfiguration with JwtProperties binding, conditional JwtUtils registration when minimall.auth.jwt.secret is configured, UserContextFilter registration with bean backoff, and Spring Boot AutoConfiguration imports.
- Changed files: common-auth/pom.xml; common-auth/src/main/java/com/minimall/common/auth/config/CommonAuthAutoConfiguration.java; common-auth/src/main/java/com/minimall/common/auth/web/UserContextFilter.java; common-auth/src/main/resources/META-INF/spring/org.springframework.boot.autoconfigure.AutoConfiguration.imports; common-auth/src/test/java/com/minimall/common/auth/config/CommonAuthAutoConfigurationTest.java; common-auth/src/test/java/com/minimall/common/auth/web/UserContextFilterTest.java; .taskmaster/tasks/tasks.json; docs/dev-log.md
- Commands run: task-master next; task-master show 5.3; task-master set-status --id=5.3 --status=in-progress; mvn -pl common-auth -am test; mvn clean package -DskipTests; task-master set-status --id=5.3 --status=done; task-master show 5
- Test result: mvn -pl common-auth -am test succeeded with common-core 12 tests passing and common-auth 26 tests passing. mvn clean package -DskipTests succeeded for the full 10-module reactor.
- Issues: WSL still prints a NAT/localhost warning after commands, but commands completed successfully.
- Next: Continue with the next TaskMaster task after running task-master next.

## Task 6.2 - Implement register and login endpoints
- Date: 2026-05-02
- Status: Done
- Implemented: Added user-service register and login APIs at POST /api/users/register and POST /api/users/login. Added validation DTOs, response DTOs, UserAuthService, UserAuthController, BCrypt PasswordEncoder configuration, JWT issuing through common-auth JwtUtils, and environment-variable JWT configuration. Registration stores BCrypt password hashes and maps duplicate usernames to BusinessException(ErrorCode.CONFLICT). Login returns a Bearer token and maps missing users or wrong passwords to the same UNAUTHORIZED response.
- Changed files: .env.example; user-service/pom.xml; user-service/src/main/resources/application.yml; user-service/src/main/java/com/minimall/user/config/UserSecurityConfig.java; user-service/src/main/java/com/minimall/user/dto/LoginRequest.java; user-service/src/main/java/com/minimall/user/dto/LoginResponse.java; user-service/src/main/java/com/minimall/user/dto/RegisterRequest.java; user-service/src/main/java/com/minimall/user/dto/UserResponse.java; user-service/src/main/java/com/minimall/user/service/UserAuthService.java; user-service/src/main/java/com/minimall/user/web/UserAuthController.java; user-service/src/test/java/com/minimall/user/web/UserAuthControllerTest.java; .taskmaster/tasks/tasks.json; docs/dev-log.md
- Commands run: task-master next; task-master show 6.2; git status --short; task-master set-status --id=6.2 --status=in-progress; source and contract reads; mvn -pl user-service -am test; mvn clean package -DskipTests
- Test result: mvn -pl user-service -am test succeeded with common-core 12 tests, common-auth 26 tests, and user-service 7 tests passing. mvn clean package -DskipTests succeeded for the full 10-module reactor.
- Issues: WSL still prints a NAT/localhost warning after commands, but commands completed successfully.
- Next: Task 6.3 - implement /me endpoint using UserContext and complete endpoint-level verification.

## Task 6.3 - Implement /me endpoint using UserContext
- Date: 2026-05-02
- Status: Done
- Implemented: Added GET /api/users/me to user-service. The endpoint reads the current UserContext from UserContextHolder, returns ApiResponse.success(CurrentUserResponse), and maps missing context to BusinessException(ErrorCode.UNAUTHORIZED, "Unauthorized"). Added endpoint-level MockMvc coverage for X-User-Id/X-Username propagation headers, Authorization Bearer JWT, missing authentication, and post-request ThreadLocal cleanup.
- Changed files: user-service/src/main/java/com/minimall/user/dto/CurrentUserResponse.java; user-service/src/main/java/com/minimall/user/web/UserAuthController.java; user-service/src/test/java/com/minimall/user/web/UserAuthControllerTest.java; .taskmaster/tasks/tasks.json; docs/dev-log.md

## Task 7.3 - Implement product detail Redis cache
- Date: 2026-05-03
- Status: Done
- Implemented: Added product detail cache-aside logic in ProductService using StringRedisTemplate and Jackson JSON serialization with key product:detail:{productId}. Detail and internal detail queries now share the cached read path. Cache misses fall back to DB and write Redis with a configurable TTL. Product update, on-shelf, and off-shelf operations delete the detail cache after transaction commit. Redis read/write/delete failures are logged and fall back to DB behavior so product APIs do not require Redis to be available for correctness.
- Changed files: product-service/src/main/java/com/minimall/product/service/ProductService.java; product-service/src/main/resources/application.yml; product-service/src/test/java/com/minimall/product/web/ProductControllerTest.java; .taskmaster/tasks/tasks.json; docs/dev-log.md

## Task 10.2 - Product validation client for order creation
- Date: 2026-05-08
- Status: Done
- Implemented: Added an order-service product validation client contract for create-order flow without depending on product-service DTOs. The client calls GET /internal/products/{productId}, maps stable ApiResponse success/error bodies, returns a local ProductSnapshot, treats missing products as BusinessException(ErrorCode.NOT_FOUND, "Product not found"), treats non-ON_SHELF products as BusinessException(ErrorCode.BAD_REQUEST, "Product is off shelf"), and normalizes downstream client failures to BusinessException(ErrorCode.INTERNAL_ERROR, "Product validation failed") without leaking downstream details. Added configurable product service base URL through PRODUCT_SERVICE_BASE_URL.
- Changed files: order-service/src/main/java/com/minimall/order/client/product/ProductApiResponse.java; order-service/src/main/java/com/minimall/order/client/product/ProductClient.java; order-service/src/main/java/com/minimall/order/client/product/ProductSnapshot.java; order-service/src/main/java/com/minimall/order/client/product/ProductStatus.java; order-service/src/main/java/com/minimall/order/client/product/ProductValidationService.java; order-service/src/main/resources/application.yml; order-service/src/test/java/com/minimall/order/client/product/ProductClientTest.java; order-service/src/test/java/com/minimall/order/client/product/ProductValidationServiceTest.java; .taskmaster/tasks/tasks.json; docs/dev-log.md

## Task 10.3 - Inventory deduct client for order creation
- Date: 2026-05-09
- Status: Done
- Implemented: Added an order-service inventory deduct client contract for the create-order flow without depending on inventory-service DTOs. The client posts InventoryDeductRequest to POST /internal/inventories/deduct, maps stable ApiResponse bodies to a local InventorySnapshot, treats insufficient inventory as BusinessException(ErrorCode.CONFLICT, "Insufficient inventory"), maps missing inventory to BusinessException(ErrorCode.NOT_FOUND, "Inventory not found"), and normalizes downstream failures to BusinessException(ErrorCode.INTERNAL_ERROR, "Inventory deduct failed") without leaking downstream details. ## Task 10.5 - Duplicate submit idempotency for create order
- Date: 2026-05-09
- Status: Done
- Implemented: Added create-order idempotency scoped by userId plus idempotencyKey. The command service now replays existing orders before external calls, uses Redis SETNX with a TTL to reject in-flight duplicate submissions with BusinessException(ErrorCode.CONFLICT, "Order creation is in progress, please retry"), leaves successful locks to expire, releases locks on failed attempts, and falls back to database unique-key replay when a concurrent insert wins the race. Changed the order idempotency unique constraint to user_id + idempotency_key and added Redis configuration for order-service.

## Development rule update - Stable WSL command discipline
- Date: 2026-05-13
- Status: Done
- Implemented: Updated AGENTS.md with a Command Reliability section to reduce PowerShell-to-WSL quoting and parsing failures. The rule now prefers short WSL commands, shallow quoting for git commit messages, apply_patch for file edits and dev-log updates, simple fixed-string searches, and explicit avoidance of long inline printf blocks, heredocs, nested quotes, pipelines, command substitution, semicolon chains, and complex grep alternation through the Windows command bridge.

- Test result: Documentation-only rule change; no Maven build required.

- Next: Future MiniMall work should follow the stable command templates in AGENTS.md before running TaskMaster, Maven, grep, git, or file-edit commands.

## Task 16.4 - Gateway request logging and Redis-backed rate limiting

## Task 17.2 - Order timeout scheduler wiring

- Status: Done
- Implemented: Enabled Spring Scheduling for order-service. Added environment-driven timeout scheduler settings under minimall.order.timeout for enabled, fixed-delay, and batch-size. ## Phase 0 Task 4.4 - Polish order and payment public DTOs
- Date: 2026-05-20
- Status: Done
- Implemented: Polished order and payment public DTO contracts so public responses expose business identifiers instead of naked database ids. Added `userId` to order create, cancel, detail, and list summary responses; added cancel `productId`; added `userId` and `productId` to payment responses by mapping `product_id` on the payment-service order read model. ## Phase 1 Task 2 - Implement API client and shared frontend types
- Date: 2026-05-22
- Status: Done
- Branch: feature/phase1-customer-frontend
- TaskMaster tag: phase1-customer-frontend
- Implemented: Built the typed Axios API client and shared frontend types for the customer storefront. All DTO field names, enum string values, error codes, and gateway paths were verified directly against backend source before writing types (not assumed from docs). Types layer: ApiResponse<T>/PageResponse<T>/PageParams, an ErrorCode string-code map (12 codes) and an ApiError class (types/api.ts); user/product/inventory/order/payment DTOs with literal-union enum types. Confirmed against source: ApiResponse.code is a numeric string ("40100"); PageResponse paging is 0-based; order list (/my) and order detail share the same shape with items: OrderItemSummary[]; CreateOrderResponse/CancelOrderResponse are flat (productId/quantity, no items[]); CreateOrderRequest.idempotencyKey is @NotBlank REQUIRED; RegisterRequest.password is @Size(min=6,max=128); LoginResponse carries tokenType; /me returns only userId+username; ProductResponse.productId is a String; BigDecimal money fields serialize as JSON number (no custom Jackson config), so price/amount/totalAmount/unitPrice are typed number. http.ts: axios instance with baseURL from VITE_API_BASE_URL, request interceptor injecting Authorization: Bearer from localStorage; response interceptor throws ApiError on 2xx success=false and routes by HTTP status (401 -> clearToken + redirect /login unless already there; 403/429/500/network -> ElMessage; other 4xx/business codes thrown for the caller to handle contextually). Identity headers (X-User-Id/X-Username) and /internal are avoided by construction. Typed get/post helpers unwrap ApiResponse.data. Endpoint modules call only canonical /api/** paths: user(register/login/me), product(list/detail), inventory(get), order(create/myOrders/get/cancel), payment(pay/get). utils/token.ts centralizes localStorage token read/write/clear for reuse by the Task 3 auth store.
- Changed files: frontend/src/types/api.ts; frontend/src/types/user.ts; frontend/src/types/product.ts; frontend/src/types/inventory.ts; frontend/src/types/order.ts; frontend/src/types/payment.ts; frontend/src/utils/token.ts; frontend/src/api/http.ts; frontend/src/api/user.ts; frontend/src/api/product.ts; frontend/src/api/inventory.ts; frontend/src/api/order.ts; frontend/src/api/payment.ts; .taskmaster/tasks/tasks.json; docs/dev-log.md

## Phase 1 Task 3 - Build routing, authentication store, and global layout
- Date: 2026-05-22
- Status: Done
- Branch: feature/phase1-customer-frontend
- TaskMaster tag: phase1-customer-frontend
- Implemented: Built the customer storefront's routing, auth state, and shared layout skeleton; business pages remain placeholder stubs deferred to their own tasks (no future-task work pulled forward). Pinia auth store (stores/auth.ts): token (initialized from localStorage via utils/token.ts), currentUser, isLoggedIn getter, and login/register/fetchCurrentUser/logout actions reusing the Task 2 api/user client. login() stores the token and sets currentUser directly from the login response (no extra /me round-trip); fetchCurrentUser() restores the username after a hard refresh when the token survives but in-memory user is gone; logout() clears both state and localStorage. Vue Router (router/index.ts) with createWebHistory and lazy-loaded views for /, /login, /register, /products, /products/:productId, /checkout, /orders, /orders/:orderNo, /payments/:orderNo, /403, and a catch-all 404; / redirects to /products; scrollBehavior resets to top. Global beforeEach guard: restores currentUser when token present but user not loaded (a 401 there is handled by the http interceptor); redirects unauthenticated access to requiresAuth routes (checkout/orders/order-detail/payment) to /login?redirect=<fullPath>; redirects logged-in users away from guestOnly routes (login/register) to /products. Shared layout: DefaultLayout.vue (AppHeader + router-view, page max-width 1200px on #f5f6f8) and AppHeader.vue (brand link, 商品 link; guests see 登录/注册; signed-in users see 我的订单, username, and a 退出 button that clears auth and routes to /login; active link highlighted in #2563eb). Placeholder views for all routes (param views show their route param for routing smoke checks; login/register stubs note Task 4). Wired router into main.ts (use order: pinia -> router -> ElementPlus) and replaced the App.vue scaffold card with DefaultLayout.

## Phase 1 Task 4 - Implement login and registration pages

## Phase 1 Task 5 (prereq) - Open catalog reads at the api-gateway for guest browsing
- Date: 2026-05-22
- Status: Done
- Branch: feature/phase1-customer-frontend
- Backend change (explicitly approved by the user): Phase 1 PRD section 4.1 requires guests (unauthenticated) to browse the product list, view product detail, and view inventory. The api-gateway's GatewayAuthenticationFilter previously bypassed authentication only for OPTIONS, non-/api/ paths, /api/users/login, and /api/users/register, so every catalog read returned 401 Missing token without a JWT - a hard contradiction with the PRD that could not be satisfied by frontend-only work. Discovered while live-verifying Task 5 against the running Docker Compose backend (GET /api/products returned 40100 without a token, 200 with one). Per CLAUDE.md (no backend changes without explicit request), surfaced the conflict and the user approved opening the read endpoints.
- Implemented: Added isPublicCatalogRead(request, path) to GatewayAuthenticationFilter, invoked from shouldBypassAuthentication. It bypasses JWT only for GET requests to /api/products, /api/products/** (detail), and /api/inventories/** (stock). All non-GET methods stay authenticated, so product create/update (POST/PUT) and on-shelf/off-shelf (POST) plus every order/payment route remain protected. Existing header sanitization still strips any spoofed X-User-Id/X-Username before the bypass, so public reads carry no forged identity. /internal/** remains blocked by GatewayInternalPathBlockFilter (unchanged).
- Changed files: api-gateway/src/main/java/com/minimall/gateway/security/GatewayAuthenticationFilter.java; api-gateway/src/test/java/com/minimall/gateway/GatewayAuthenticationFilterTest.java; api-gateway/src/test/java/com/minimall/gateway/GatewayIntegrationRegressionTest.java; docs/dev-log.md
- Commands run: read of ProductController/InventoryController mappings (only GET list+detail and GET /{productId} are reads; mutations are POST/PUT) and GatewayAuthConfig; mvn -pl api-gateway -am test; mvn -pl api-gateway -am package -DskipTests; docker compose --env-file .env.example --profile services up -d --build api-gateway; anonymous curl smokes for products/inventories (GET) and products POST + orders/my GET (must stay 401)
- Test result: mvn -pl api-gateway test passed 30/30 (4 new auth-filter cases: public product list strips spoofed headers, public product detail bypass, public inventory bypass, product POST still 401; plus the GatewayIntegrationRegressionTest updated so product/inventory GET are public reads keyed ip:unknown rather than protected user:42 routes). After repackaging the jar and rebuilding the gateway image, live curl confirmed anonymous GET /api/products and GET /api/inventories/{id} return 200 with data, while anonymous POST /api/products and GET /api/orders/my still return 401 Missing token.
- Issues: The first image rebuild served stale code because infra/docker/java-service.Dockerfile only copies a prebuilt target/*.jar (no in-container compile); running mvn test alone did not refresh the jar. Fixed by mvn package before docker build. The IDE flags @RequestMapping on the tests' TestDownstreamController as a non-precise mapping, but it intentionally handles both GET and POST for the downstream stub, so it is left as-is.

## Phase 1 Task 6 - Implement product detail and inventory display
- Date: 2026-05-23

- Implemented: Replaced the ProductDetailView placeholder with the customer product detail page at /products/:productId, backed by the Task 2 product/inventory api clients (no changes to api/product.ts/api/inventory.ts/router/types - consume only). On mount loads product (GET /api/products/{productId}) and inventory (GET /api/inventories/{productId}) concurrently via Promise.allSettled so a transient inventory error does not blank out the product detail (and vice-versa); reloads on productId param change for in-route SPA navigation. Two-column layout (el-row md 14/10, stacked on xs): left card shows name, status tag (在售 / 已下架), price (¥X.XX, red 28px), productId meta, and the description with whitespace-pre-wrap; right card shows the stockState as a localized tag (IN_STOCK 有货 success / OUT_OF_STOCK 无货 danger / INACTIVE 未上架 info), availableStock and lockedStock rows, then a quantity selector (el-input-number, min=1, max=availableStock or 1 when none, precision 0, step 1, disabled when product off-shelf / no inventory / not IN_STOCK) and a full-width 立即下单 primary button. canOrder requires product ON_SHELF AND inventory present AND stockState IN_STOCK AND quantity integer in [1, availableStock]; quantity is also clamped via a watcher whenever availableStock changes so a refresh that lowers stock cannot leave a stale invalid value. Disabled reason is surfaced under the button (off-shelf > inventory unavailable > INACTIVE > OUT_OF_STOCK/availableStock<=0 > quantity out of range) so the user sees why the button is greyed. Three terminal states beyond success: (a) 404/PRODUCT_NOT_FOUND -> el-result icon=warning '商品不存在' + 返回商品列表; (b) other product load error -> el-result error + 重试 + 返回; (c) inventory-only error -> inline el-alert + small 重试加载库存 button inside the right card, leaving the rest of the page visible. onOrder gates by auth.isLoggedIn: unauthenticated users go to /login?redirect=<route.fullPath> (so the guard restores them right back); authenticated users go to /checkout?productId=...&quantity=... (the /checkout page itself remains the Task 7 placeholder and is not wired up to POST /api/orders yet).

## Phase 1 Task 7 - Implement checkout and idempotent order creation
- Date: 2026-05-23
- Status: Done
- Branch: feature/phase1-customer-frontend
- TaskMaster tag: phase1-customer-frontend
- Implemented: Replaced the CheckoutView placeholder with the protected checkout page at /checkout?productId=...&quantity=..., consuming the Task 2 product/inventory/order api clients only (no changes to api/order.ts/types/order.ts/router/http/auth - the route was already requiresAuth and the api client already exposes createOrder). Query-param parsing rejects missing productId, non-integer quantity, and quantity < 1 with an el-result '参数无效' state so a hand-crafted URL can't slip through to a malformed POST. On mount loads product and inventory concurrently via Promise.allSettled (same error policy as the detail page: product failure replaces the whole layout; inventory-only failure shows an inline el-alert + retry inside the summary card without blanking the rest). idempotencyKey lifecycle: ONE crypto.randomUUID() generated in onMounted and stored on a ref, reused for every retry of the same submit attempt, regenerated only when the component remounts (i.e. when the user re-enters /checkout) - the Task 7 contract. crypto.randomUUID falls back to a Date.now+Math.random concat for the few browsers that still lack it. Single-card summary layout (max-width 720px, centered): 商品名称 / 商品编号 (monospace) / 单价 / 数量 / divider / 可售库存 (or inventory error) / divider / 合计 (¥X.XX, red 28px) + small '订单最终金额以后端结算为准' caption clarifying the total is display-only and the backend recomputes the authoritative amount. Submit gating (canSubmit): submitting AND product ON_SHELF AND inventory present AND stockState IN_STOCK AND 1 <= quantity <= availableStock; disabled-reason hint mirrors the detail page priority order (off-shelf > inventory unavailable > INACTIVE > OUT_OF_STOCK > quantity out of range). On click: submitting=true -> POST /api/orders -> success -> router.replace({name:'order-detail', orderNo}) (replace not push, so the back button cannot return to the now-stale checkout page and risk a double-submit); on failure -> submitting=false, inline el-alert shows the backend message, idempotencyKey is INTENTIONALLY NOT regenerated so a retry hits the same idempotency window. Network/401/403/429/500 still surfaces a global ElMessage toast via the http interceptor; business-code errors (e.g. insufficient stock) come through as the inline alert. 取消 button routes back to the product detail page (or product list if productId is missing). 立即下单 navigation from the Task 6 detail page is unchanged - this task only wires up the destination.
- Changed files: frontend/src/views/CheckoutView.vue; .taskmaster/tasks/tasks.json; docs/dev-log.md
- Commands run: node read of .taskmaster/tasks/tasks.json for Task 7 scope; reads of router/api/order.ts/types/order.ts/types/api.ts/api/product.ts/api/inventory.ts/CheckoutView.vue placeholder to verify the contract before editing; npm run build; ss -ltn :5173 probe; for the race-condition business-error test (#10) the assistant drove a curl flow: registered an e2e-drain user, logged in to capture the JWT, POST /api/orders with quantity = current availableStock to drain stock to OUT_OF_STOCK, then POST /api/orders/{orderNo}/cancel to release after the user observed the inline error in the browser; spot-checks of GET /api/inventories/PHASE0-SMOKE-20260521 confirmed avail+locked totals stay constant at the seeded 50 across every snapshot (no inventory leak); reads of order-service OrderTimeoutScheduler + payment-expire-seconds (=900s) to explain to the user why PENDING_PAYMENT test orders auto-release in the background
- Test result: npm run build (vue-tsc --noEmit + vite build) passed; CheckoutView emits as its own lazy chunk (6.19 kB). Full manual browser smoke run by the user against the running Docker Compose backend covered all 10 cases from the test plan: (1) detail->checkout query roundtrip + correct total, (2) submit success -> /orders/{orderNo}, (3) network-offline retry reuses the same idempotencyKey UUID (verified by comparing Network Payload of failed then successful POSTs with Preserve log), (4) re-entering /checkout generates a NEW key (verified across two separate checkout entries), (5) rapid double-click only fires one POST, (6) unauthenticated deep-link goes to /login?redirect=/checkout?... and the guard restores the URL after login, (7) missing / non-integer / zero quantity -> '参数无效', (8) non-existent productId -> '商品不存在', (9) over-stock quantity in URL -> button disabled with range hint, (10) RACE: with a /checkout page already loaded for qty=1, the assistant drained available stock to 0 via e2e-drain user's curl; the user's click then returned the backend's business error inline (el-alert) without leaving the page, and a second click retried with the same idempotencyKey - confirming the inline error path and the no-regen-on-failure policy. Backend invariant verified: availableStock + lockedStock stayed at the seeded total of 50 throughout the entire test session (45+5 -> 0+50 (during drain) -> 47+3 (after cancel + auto-expiry of 2 stale orders) -> 48+2 (one more stale order auto-expired) - i.e. inventory is conserved and the OrderTimeoutScheduler 60-second job + 15-min payment-expire-seconds window are functioning correctly. No type errors or runtime console errors observed.

The summary's 合计 is computed client-side from price*quantity and is display-only - the backend recomputes authoritatively, and the caption tells the user so. The /orders/{orderNo} destination is still the Task 8 placeholder, so success-navigation lands on the placeholder page; that's expected and Task 8 will replace it.

## Phase 1 Task 8 - Implement my orders order detail and cancellation
- Date: 2026-05-23
- Status: Done
- Branch: feature/phase1-customer-frontend
- TaskMaster tag: phase1-customer-frontend
- Implemented: Replaced the OrdersView and OrderDetailView placeholders with the customer-facing "我的订单" surface backed by Task 2's typed order api client only (no changes to api/order.ts/types/order.ts/router/http/auth - the routes were already requiresAuth and listMyOrders/getOrder/cancelOrder were already wired). New shared util frontend/src/utils/order-status.ts: getOrderStatusMeta(status) maps each OrderStatus enum value to a Chinese label + Element Plus tag type (PENDING_PAYMENT 待支付/warning, PAID 已支付/success, CANCELLED 已取消/info, CLOSED 已关闭/info, REFUNDED 已退款/danger) with a defensive fallback (raw status + info type) so an unknown backend value never crashes the page. Reused by both views so status copy/color cannot drift between list and detail. OrdersView (/orders): reads ?page= from the URL query (1-based UI <-> 0-based backend, PAGE_SIZE 10), card-list layout consistent with the storefront brief instead of an admin table; each card shows the monospace orderNo, status tag, product summary line (first item productName x quantity, "等 N 件" when items.length > 1, dash when empty), totalAmount in red ¥ format, createdAt, and (only for PENDING_PAYMENT) the expireAt as 支付截止. Per-card actions: PENDING_PAYMENT shows 取消订单 + 去支付 (the latter routes to {name:'payment', params:{orderNo}}); all other statuses show 查看详情. Whole card click goes to the detail page; button clicks use @click.stop so they do not double-navigate. Four states: v-loading during fetch, el-empty "暂无订单" + 去逛逛 CTA -> /products, el-result error + retry on failure, and the list itself. el-pagination (background, prev/pager/next/jumper/total) is rendered only when totalElements > PAGE_SIZE; page changes router.replace({query:{page}}) without history stacking, and a watch on route.query.page re-fetches on browser back/forward. After a cancel succeeds the list reloads; if the current page goes empty (last order on a page cancelled) the view backs off to the new last available page automatically. OrderDetailView (/orders/:orderNo): loads on mount and on orderNo param change. Layout: detail head with title + monospace orderNo on the left and a large status tag on the right; "基本信息" card grid showing 下单时间, 更新时间, plus status-conditional rows (支付截止 only for PENDING_PAYMENT, 支付时间 only for PAID, 关闭时间 only for CANCELLED/CLOSED); "商品明细" card listing each OrderItemSummary as productName + monospace productId, x quantity, unit price, subtotal (unitPrice * quantity), with an el-divider then the 合计 row (¥X.XX, red 28px) and a "订单金额以后端结算为准" caption. Bottom actions: PENDING_PAYMENT shows 取消订单 + 去支付; everything else shows 返回订单列表. Shared cancel flow in both views: ElMessageBox.confirm("确定要取消订单 {orderNo} 吗？此操作无法恢复", "取消订单", {type:'warning', 确认取消/再想想}) -> cancelOrder(orderNo) -> ElMessage.success('订单已取消') + reload current data; dialog dismiss is silently ignored (Promise rejection path) so no spurious toast. Business-conflict handling: ApiError.code === ORDER_INVALID_STATE (40902) or ORDER_CANCELLED (40901) -> ElMessage.warning('订单状态已变化，已为你刷新最新数据') + reload, so the user always sees the authoritative current state even when their UI was stale. Other business codes surface via ElMessage.error with the backend message; network/401/429/500 are still toasted by the http interceptor. Per-card cancel spinner is keyed by cancellingOrderNo so simultaneous cards do not all spin.
- Mid-task contract refinement: User observed that hitting another user's orderNo returned 404 '订单不存在' rather than 403. Reading order-service/.../OrderQueryService.java:28-29 confirmed this is intentional: the backend queries by composite (orderNo, userId) and throws NOT_FOUND for both "does not exist" and "exists but belongs to another user" - an authorization-aware 404 to prevent attackers from enumerating valid orderNos by observing 403/404 differences (the same pattern GitHub/AWS S3/Stripe use). The frontend's 403 branch in OrderDetailView was therefore dead code for this endpoint. Per CLAUDE.md ("Don't add error handling for scenarios that can't happen" / "Trust internal code and framework guarantees") and with explicit user approval, removed the loadError 'forbidden' variant, the 403 detection in the catch block, and the corresponding el-result block; added a one-line comment in the catch block documenting the authorization-aware 404 contract so future maintainers don't reintroduce a 403 branch.
- Changed files: frontend/src/utils/order-status.ts (NEW); frontend/src/views/OrdersView.vue; frontend/src/views/OrderDetailView.vue; .taskmaster/tasks/tasks.json; docs/dev-log.md
- Commands run: node read of .taskmaster/tasks/tasks.json for Task 8 scope; reads of OrdersView/OrderDetailView placeholders, api/order.ts, types/order.ts, types/api.ts (ErrorCode constants) before editing; npm run build (twice - initial implementation and after the 403-branch removal); read of order-service OrderQueryService.java to confirm the backend's NOT_FOUND-for-cross-user behavior is deliberate; ss -ltn :5173 probe; anonymous curl --noproxy '*' http://localhost:8080/api/inventories/PHASE0-SMOKE-20260521 to confirm backend still healthy
- Test result: npm run build (vue-tsc --noEmit + vite build) passed; OrdersView lazy chunk 4.55 kB, OrderDetailView 5.83 kB, order-status util 0.29 kB. Full manual browser smoke against the running Docker Compose backend by the user covered all 14 cases (originally 15 - cases #10 and #11 collapsed into one "order-not-found-or-not-yours" path after the contract refinement): list display + status tag colors, button visibility gated on PENDING_PAYMENT only, cancel-with-confirm dialog (confirm + dismiss paths), per-card cancel spinner + list refresh, whole-card click vs button @click.stop, detail full-field rendering with status-conditional time fields, detail cancel reload, 去支付 navigation to the Task 9 placeholder, 404/cross-user both showing '订单不存在', empty-list state on a fresh account, ?page= URL sync + browser back/forward, unauthenticated guard redirect to /login?redirect=. No type errors, no runtime console errors.
- Issues: The pre-existing Element Plus full-import main-chunk >500kB warning persists (out of scope). The cancel-conflict 40901/40902 path was not exercised live (would require either two browser sessions cancelling concurrently or hitting a natural 15-min expiry mid-cancel); the handler is covered by construction - same try/catch shape as the verified cancel-success path - and surfaces 'ElMessage.warning + reload'. The 去支付 destination is the Task 9 placeholder; Task 9 will replace it. ## Phase 1 Task 9 - Implement simulated payment flow
- Date: 2026-05-23
- Status: Done
- Branch: feature/phase1-customer-frontend
- TaskMaster tag: phase1-customer-frontend
- Implemented: Replaced the PaymentView placeholder with the protected /payments/:orderNo page, consuming the Task 2 order + payment api clients only (no changes to api/payment.ts/types/payment.ts/api/order.ts/router/http/auth - the route was already requiresAuth and payOrder/getPayment/getOrder were already wired). Page is driven by an explicit ViewState union: loading | error-not-found | error-generic | ready | submitting | success | success-pending | already-paid | not-payable - chosen so each branch in the template renders independently and there is no state I cannot describe to a reviewer in one word. On mount: generates a single crypto.randomUUID idempotencyKey (re-used across retries, reset on remount - consistent with checkout's contract); calls getOrder(orderNo); routes by order.status: PAID -> already-paid (also tries getPayment and tolerates a missing record without erroring); PENDING_PAYMENT -> ready; everything else (CANCELLED/CLOSED/REFUNDED) -> not-payable. Authorization-aware 404 (Task 8's contract) is reused here: cross-user or missing orderNo both surface as error-not-found. Top-of-page el-alert banner permanently declares '模拟支付 ... 不会发生真实扣款' so the demo-only nature is visible in every state. Shared 'order info' card across states shows orderNo (monospace), status tag (Task 8's shared util keeps the label/color identical with the rest of the app), 支付截止 (only for ready/submitting), and the 应付金额 in red 28px. READY state: 返回订单详情 + 主按钮 '确认支付 ¥X.XX'; on submit -> submitting state, payOrder({channel:'MOCK', idempotencyKey}). After /pay returns SUCCESS, pollOrderUntilPaid() polls GET /api/orders/{orderNo} up to 5 times at 800ms intervals (≤4s wall-clock) because the order-service flips to PAID only after consuming the RabbitMQ PaymentSuccessEvent published by payment-service - the polling exists specifically to hide that async window from the customer. Inner errors during polling are swallowed so a transient blip doesn't abort the whole flow; the loop's exit condition is the authoritative signal. On PAID detected -> refresh getPayment for the receipt and -> success. If 5 polls all observe a non-PAID status -> success-pending (the payment IS accepted, just the order projection lags); shows an info el-alert and a '再次刷新订单' button that re-runs pollOrderUntilPaid (so a user who waits a bit can get to the final state without a hard reload). SUCCESS state: large green check icon + '支付成功' headline + '模拟支付' clarification, followed by the payment receipt rows (paymentNo monospace, channel MOCK, amount, paidAt) when available, and two CTAs (查看订单详情 / 继续逛逛). ALREADY-PAID state: green el-alert + receipt + 查看订单详情 button (no pay button - the task description explicitly forbids paying when not PENDING_PAYMENT). NOT-PAYABLE state: info el-alert quoting the localized status label + 返回订单列表/详情. PAYMENT_ALREADY_SUCCESS (40903) is caught explicitly during submit: instead of leaving the user with a stuck inline error, the handler ElMessage.warning's + re-calls loadInitial so the page silently transitions to already-paid (typical case: two tabs paying the same order, second one races and loses; first one's success is now visible everywhere). All other submit errors surface as an inline el-alert above the action row, and the idempotencyKey is NOT regenerated so a follow-up retry hits the same dedup window. Component lifetime: a `cancelled` flag is flipped in onBeforeUnmount and is checked before every state assignment after an awaited operation, so navigating away mid-poll doesn't write to a torn-down component (Vue 3 would warn or set state on a stale instance otherwise).
- Changed files: frontend/src/views/PaymentView.vue; .taskmaster/tasks/tasks.json; docs/dev-log.md
- Commands run: node read of .taskmaster/tasks/tasks.json for Task 9 scope; reads of PaymentView placeholder, api/payment.ts, types/payment.ts, types/api.ts (ErrorCode for PAYMENT_ALREADY_SUCCESS), router, OrderQueryService.java (to reconfirm authorization-aware 404 for /api/orders/{orderNo}); grep of order-service/payment-service for PaymentSuccessEvent wiring (confirmed payment-service.../PaymentEventPublisher.java publishes and order-service.../PaymentSuccessEventConsumer.java is a @RabbitListener that flips the order to PAID); npm run build; ss -ltn :5173 probe; anonymous curl --noproxy '*' http://localhost:8080/api/inventories/PHASE0-SMOKE-20260521 to confirm backend reachable
- Test result: npm run build (vue-tsc --noEmit + vite build) passed; PaymentView emits as its own lazy chunk (8.89 kB). Manual browser smoke against the running Docker Compose backend by the user covered cases #1-#11 from the test plan: full happy-path payment with the 800ms*5 poll loop observably catching the order's PAID transition on the first or second poll tick; '⚠ 模拟支付' banner visible in every state; idempotencyKey + channel='MOCK' present in the POST body; already-paid landing path; not-payable (CANCELLED) landing path; authorization-aware 404; unauthenticated redirect via router guard; double-click protection; the 40903 PAYMENT_ALREADY_SUCCESS race handler. No type errors, no runtime console errors.
- Issues: The pre-existing Element Plus full-import main-chunk >500kB warning persists (out of scope). Case #12 (polling-timeout success-pending fallback) was NOT exercised live - it requires either stopping order-service mid-flow or otherwise breaking the PaymentSuccessEvent consumer so the order never flips to PAID; covered by construction (pollOrderUntilPaid returns false after 5 attempts -> state.value = 'success-pending' branch with manual refresh CTA), but not observed end-to-end. If we want this verified live later, the cleanest setup is docker compose stop order-service after submitting; alternatively a unit test could simulate the timing. The 40901/40902-equivalent for the payment endpoint was not separately mapped because the backend's payment-pay errors are surfaced via the inline el-alert and the http interceptor's existing toast pipeline; only PAYMENT_ALREADY_SUCCESS has a state-transition meaning and is therefore the only code with a bespoke branch. Polling uses a generic setTimeout sleep; no exponential backoff because 800ms*5 is small and bounded - any longer waits should prefer the manual-refresh button in success-pending.
- Next: Phase 1 Task 10 - Acceptance testing, UX polish, and documentation.

- Mid-task regression fix (single line, frontend-only, recorded with explicit user approval): The Task 8 OrdersView was calling listMyOrders with only {page, size} - no sort. The backend OrderController.myOrders(Pageable) does not declare a @PageableDefault, so Spring forwarded an unsorted Pageable and the repository's findByUserId returned rows in primary-key ASC order (oldest first), surfacing as "newest order is at the bottom" during the live E2E. Fixed in frontend/src/views/OrdersView.vue:39 by adding sort: 'createdAt,desc' to the listMyOrders params; PageParams already supported the field (types/api.ts:19), backend Pageable resolver auto-parses sort=createdAt,desc with no backend change. Per the Phase 1 boundary (CLAUDE.md "do not modify backend business logic unless explicitly requested") the fix is frontend-only; the backend default is left intact because changing it would silently rewrite the contract for any other current/future caller. Documented in the acceptance doc Section 5 (API contract row for /api/orders/my). type-check (vue-tsc --noEmit) passed; user verified /orders now lists newest first via HMR refresh without restarting Vite.
- Changed files: docs/phase1-frontend-acceptance.md (NEW); frontend/README.md (sections added); README.md (Documentation Map entries); frontend/src/views/OrdersView.vue (one-line sort fix); .taskmaster/tasks/tasks.json (Task 10 done, completedCount 10); docs/dev-log.md (this entry)

## Phase 1 follow-up - Handle route reuse in checkout and payment + add Vitest
- Date: 2026-05-23
- Status: Done (post-Phase 1 hardening; not a TaskMaster task - Phase 1 was already 10/10 at this point)
- Branch: feature/phase1-customer-frontend
- Commit: b1e5768
- Background: A code review of the shipped Phase 1 frontend surfaced two same-component route-reuse risks that the end-of-phase manual E2E happened to miss because the test flow never navigated /payments/A -> /payments/B or /checkout?productId=A -> /checkout?productId=B without unmounting in between. Both PaymentView and CheckoutView ran their data load + idempotencyKey generation only in onMounted, so Vue Router's component-reuse optimisation could leave the user looking at the previous order/product while the URL pointed to the new one, and a submit-with-stale-data window existed during query transitions. This commit closes both holes and adds a Vitest harness so the regressions stay closed.
- Implemented:
  - PaymentView: introduced an activeRunId counter that "owns" the currently-active load attempt. loadInitial bumps activeRunId at entry and captures myRun; every awaited result (getOrder, getPayment, payOrder, the polling loop's sleeps + repeated getOrder) re-checks (myRun !== activeRunId) before writing state and bails on mismatch. pollOrderUntilPaid and refreshPaymentReceipt now take myRun as a parameter so the same run-id flows through the whole pay submit chain. The previous `cancelled` boolean is gone - onBeforeUnmount just bumps activeRunId, which makes every in-flight await fail the check at the next write site. A new `watch(() => orderNo.value, ...)` re-runs the load and regenerates idempotencyKey when the route param changes; the implicit activeRunId bump inside loadInitial invalidates any prev-orderNo writes still pending.
  - CheckoutView: same activeRunId pattern across loadAll, loadProduct, loadInventory and onSubmit. A new `watch([productIdParam, quantityParam], ...)` bumps activeRunId, resets product / inventory / errors / submitting, regenerates idempotencyKey, and only triggers loadAll when the new params are valid; invalid params just flip the existing 参数无效 branch without reloading. onSubmit now explicitly refuses to fire when `product.value.productId !== productIdParam.value` so a stale submit during a query change cannot reach the backend. The "retries reuse the same key; new entry / new query regenerates" idempotency contract from Task 7 is preserved by tying key regeneration to component remount OR a query change, not to retry attempts.
- Tests (new): Added Vitest with @vue/test-utils + happy-dom. vite.config.ts gains a `test` block (environment: 'happy-dom', globals: true, include: src/**/*.{test,spec}.ts) using vitest/config types. New scripts: `test` (vitest run) and `test:watch` (vitest). Two specs live under frontend/src/views/__tests__/: PaymentView.spec.ts (4 tests) and CheckoutView.spec.ts (5 tests). Each spec mocks vue-router with a Vue reactive() route and exposes it back via an __testRoute export so the test can mutate params/query and trigger the component's watchers; api modules and crypto.randomUUID are stubbed per-test. crypto.randomUUID is driven by a shared `currentKey` token that tests flip between phases so the component captures the value the test expects when it calls generateKey() - we cannot assert call counts because Element Plus itself calls crypto.randomUUID for internal IDs. Coverage per view: initial-mount load with the right argument; route/query change reloads with the new argument and the page no longer shows the old data; submit posts the current orderNo/productId with the regenerated idempotencyKey; CheckoutView only: invalid params skip the load and createOrder; both: a stale-in-flight async load is silently dropped when the runId has moved on. `enableAutoUnmount(afterEach)` from @vue/test-utils ensures previous-test components don't keep listening to mockRoute mutations.
- Changed files: frontend/package.json (vitest deps + scripts); frontend/package-lock.json (lockfile); frontend/vite.config.ts (test block + triple-slash reference); frontend/src/views/PaymentView.vue (runId + watch + async guards); frontend/src/views/CheckoutView.vue (runId + watch + identity check on submit); frontend/src/views/__tests__/PaymentView.spec.ts (NEW); frontend/src/views/__tests__/CheckoutView.spec.ts (NEW); docs/dev-log.md (this entry)
- Commands run: read of every customer view + router/api/types files to confirm the contract before editing; `npm install --save-dev vitest @vue/test-utils happy-dom` (added 81 packages, no funding prompts); two iterations of `npm run test` (first iteration: 5 of 9 failed - Element Plus internal crypto.randomUUID calls confused call-count assertions, and previously-mounted wrappers were still listening to mockRoute mutations across tests; fixed by switching to currentKey token + enableAutoUnmount; second iteration: 9/9 pass); `npm run type-check` clean; `npm run build` clean with chunk profile shift (CheckoutView 6.19 kB -> 6.64 kB, PaymentView 8.89 kB -> 9.27 kB - small growth from the runId + watch + async guards is expected); 4 security greps over frontend/src/ (X-User-Id|X-Username, /internal/, 8101|8102|8103|8104|8105|8106) all 0 matches; `git status` to confirm the staged set is exactly the 7 expected files; commit with the message `fix(frontend): handle route reuse in checkout and payment`
- Test result: 9/9 vitest tests pass (~800ms total wall-clock); vue-tsc --noEmit clean; vite build clean. PaymentView chunk grew 4.3% (8.89 -> 9.27 kB), CheckoutView grew 7.3% (6.19 -> 6.64 kB) - acceptable for the added defensiveness. No type errors, no runtime warnings during tests. Security grep set still 0 matches.
- Issues: None new. The pre-existing Element Plus full-import main-chunk >500 kB warning persists (out of scope, recorded since Tasks 5-9). The PaymentView polling-timeout (success-pending) path and the cancel-conflict 40901/40902 path remain not-exercised-live; the runId guards now also protect these paths against route reuse, but the underlying business-state limits documented in docs/phase1-frontend-acceptance.md Section 11 are unchanged.
- Next: No follow-up needed. Phase 1 customer frontend is complete and hardened. The acceptance doc still reflects shipped behavior; a future Phase will live under a new TaskMaster tag.

## Phase 1 UI rework — A1 Tokens & global base
- Date: 2026-05-24
- Status: Done
- Branch: feature/phase1-customer-frontend
- TaskMaster tag: phase1-customer-frontend (no TaskMaster ID — UI rework is a post-Phase-1 follow-up effort governed by docs/phase1-ui-redesign.md, not a TaskMaster task. Phase 1 was already 10/10 at start of this work.)
- Scope: First step of the Phase 1 customer frontend visual/UX rework. Establishes the design-system foundation (CSS custom properties, global base layer, type utility classes, font loading) without touching any user-facing page. Per the redesign brief (docs/phase1-ui-redesign.md §8 Phase A1), A1 is required to be a zero-visual-regression step so the foundation can be reviewed independently of the page rewrites that follow in Phase B.
- Implemented:
  - NEW frontend/src/styles/tokens.css (~115 lines) — declares the full design-system token surface as :root CSS custom properties, per the brief §2: 12 color tokens (ink-900/700/500/300/100, canvas/canvas-darker/surface, accent-terracotta + accent-terracotta-soft, success + success-soft, warn, danger + danger-soft) committing to the "ink + warm paper + single terracotta accent" voice; 3 font-family stacks (--font-sans with Inter + zh fallbacks, --font-display with Inter Tight, --font-mono); type scale variables for display-xl / display / h1 / h2 / body / body-strong / caption / mono-sm / price-md / price-lg / amount-display / brand with size, line-height, weight, and letter-spacing where defined; 10 spacing tokens on the 4px base step (4/8/12/16/20/24/32/48/64/96); 5 radius tokens (sm 6 / default 10 / md 12 / lg 16 / xl 24); 4 shadow tokens (shadow-1/2/3 + shadow-press for the focus ring); 4 motion tokens (--ease, --ease-in, --dur-1 120ms press / --dur-2 220ms hover/page-fade / --dur-3 420ms number-tween / --dur-4 800ms success ceremony). File is declaration-only — no rules apply to any selector — so importing it cannot visually change any existing page.
  - NEW frontend/src/styles/base.css (~95 lines) — global base layer per brief §2.3: box-sizing reset on *,*::before,*::after; margin/padding zero on html/body and common typographic blocks (h1-h6, p, figure, blockquote, dl, dd, ul, ol); text-size-adjust 100% on html; body adopts --font-sans + --t-body-size + var(--ink-700) text + var(--canvas) background + antialiased font smoothing + optimizeLegibility text rendering; img/svg/video/canvas/audio/iframe/embed/object set to display:block + max-width:100% to prevent inline-image baseline gaps; button reset to inherit font/color and strip native chrome; a inherits color and removes underline; :focus-visible binds a soft inset ring via var(--shadow-press) for keyboard nav only (mouse clicks are not affected); ::selection uses --accent-terracotta-soft fill with --ink-900 text; scrollbar styled via both scrollbar-width/scrollbar-color (firefox) and ::-webkit-scrollbar (chromium/safari) with a 10px track, transparent background, --ink-300 thumb darkening to --ink-500 on hover. **Important visual choice:** body's --canvas background WOULD be visible if it weren't already covered by DefaultLayout's `min-height:100vh; background:#f5f6f8` rule, which still wins on the surface area users see. This keeps A1 visually-quiet on existing pages — the canvas color will only become visible after A2 replaces the shell. Confirmed by inspection of layouts/DefaultLayout.vue.
  - NEW frontend/src/styles/typography.css (~120 lines) — utility classes (.text-display-xl, .text-display, .text-h1, .text-h2, .text-body, .text-body-strong, .text-caption, .text-mono-sm, .text-price-md, .text-price-lg, .text-amount-display, .text-brand, .tabular-nums) wiring the type-scale tokens from tokens.css into reusable class selectors. .text-price-md / .text-price-lg / .text-amount-display force tabular-nums via font-variant-numeric so columns of prices and amounts align cleanly across cards. The .tabular-nums standalone utility is provided for ad-hoc uses (order count badges, time-remaining chips). These classes are inert until a view chooses to apply them — they cannot affect any current page.
  - MODIFIED frontend/src/main.ts — added 3 new style imports (./styles/tokens.css, ./styles/base.css, ./styles/typography.css) placed AFTER `import 'element-plus/dist/index.css'`. A 5-line comment block above the imports records the cascade-direction reasoning (our overrides must come after EP so :root variables and global base styles win) and explicitly states that Phase A1 does NOT yet override Element Plus variables (deferred to end of Phase B). This is a correction relative to the initial draft of docs/phase1-ui-redesign.md, which had said "before" — both the file and the brief have now been updated.
  - MODIFIED frontend/index.html — added <link rel="preconnect"> to fonts.googleapis.com and fonts.gstatic.com (with crossorigin on the gstatic link as Google recommends), plus a single <link rel="stylesheet"> loading Inter (400/500/600/700) and Inter Tight (600/700) with display=swap. If Google Fonts is unreachable, the --font-sans / --font-display stacks fall back to PingFang SC / Hiragino Sans GB / Microsoft YaHei / system-ui — no broken rendering, just system fonts. The Inter Tight subset is intentionally narrow (only 600/700) because Inter Tight is only used for display/brand/amount text in the brief.
  - MODIFIED docs/phase1-ui-redesign.md §8 Phase A1 — synced two corrections so the brief and the implementation stay aligned: (1) clarified that style imports load AFTER Element Plus, with a parenthetical note that the earlier "before" was a cascade-direction error; (2) explicitly removed the "minimal EP variable override" from A1 and deferred it to the end of Phase B, restating A1's zero-visual-regression commitment. Also clarified that font loading happens via Google Fonts <link> tags in index.html with system-font fallbacks.
- Decisions and trade-offs:
  - A1 deliberately does NOT touch Element Plus CSS variables. The brief originally placed "minimal EP override for el-message / el-message-box / el-form-item" in A1; this was tightened to the end of Phase B during the pre-A1 plan-confirmation round so A1 can be reviewed as a pure no-op-on-pages change. This means toast and dialog colors will still match the EP default until the end of Phase B; that mismatch is acknowledged and accepted.
  - Style imports are placed AFTER `import 'element-plus/dist/index.css'`. CSS cascade direction requires our :root tokens (and any future overrides) to load last so they win.
  - DefaultLayout's existing `background: #f5f6f8` still wins over body's --canvas. This is intentional for A1 — the new canvas color will become visible only after A2 replaces the shell. Verified visually by inspecting layouts/DefaultLayout.vue.
  - Type tokens use rem-style separation (--t-{role}-size / -lh / -weight / -track) so a single token name maps to a single CSS variable, keeping utility classes simple. No fluid type (clamp()) yet — fixed sizes match the brief and avoid surprises at edge widths.
  - Google Fonts chosen over self-hosted to keep this commit small. If the user later wants to remove the CDN dependency, the change is a localized swap of the <link> tag for a self-hosted @font-face block in tokens.css or a sibling fonts.css. The --font-sans / --font-display fallback chain stays valid either way.
- Changed files: frontend/src/styles/tokens.css (NEW); frontend/src/styles/base.css (NEW); frontend/src/styles/typography.css (NEW); frontend/src/main.ts (3 imports + 5-line comment); frontend/index.html (3 <link> tags); docs/phase1-ui-redesign.md (Phase A1 paragraph synced); docs/dev-log.md (this entry); docs/phase1-ui-redesign.md is also newly tracked from the prior conversation (it was untracked before this commit).
- Commands run: read of docs/phase1-ui-redesign.md (full file) + frontend/src/main.ts + frontend/index.html + frontend/src/App.vue + frontend/src/layouts/DefaultLayout.vue to confirm the integration surface and the existing background-color cover before drafting tokens.css; ls frontend/src/styles to confirm the styles/ dir does not exist; `git status` + `git branch --show-current` at start (clean, on feature/phase1-customer-frontend); `tail -60 docs/dev-log.md` to confirm the exact dev-log entry format used by Tasks 7-10 and the route-reuse follow-up; cd frontend && `npm run build` (vue-tsc + vite, exit 0, ~4.0s); `npx vitest run` (9/9 pass, ~1.0s); `git diff --stat` + `git status` + `git ls-files --others --exclude-standard` to confirm the staged set is exactly what was planned.
- Test result: npm run build (vue-tsc --noEmit + vite build) passed cleanly. Chunk profile is essentially unchanged from the route-reuse commit b1e5768: PaymentView 9.27 kB, CheckoutView 6.64 kB, ProductDetailView 5.87 kB (all byte-identical to the previous build), OrderDetailView 5.41 kB (vs 5.83 kB before — a rollup-hash-driven drop with no source change; OrderDetailView.vue was not edited in this commit, confirmed via `git diff --stat`). The main bundle index-DAqoitjG.js stays at 1082.99 kB (the long-standing EP full-import warning persists, out of scope). Index CSS is 363.12 kB — the +2-3 kB combined size of tokens/base/typography is folded into Vite's global stylesheet at build time. Vitest: 9/9 pass in ~1.0s wall-clock (PaymentView.spec 4/4, CheckoutView.spec 5/5) — no regression on the route-reuse harness from the previous follow-up. No type errors, no runtime warnings.
- Visual smoke (mental walkthrough, not exercised live in dev server this round): the body's new --canvas background sits behind DefaultLayout's #f5f6f8 and is not visible; AppHeader is still #ffffff with #ebeef5 bottom border; ProductCard is still white card + el-tag + #f56c6c red price; LoginView is still 420px centered white card; PaymentView still shows the yellow demo banner + label-value rows. No new utility class is applied to any view, so visually pages render exactly as they did before. The font stack on body changes from the platform default to Inter, but only in places that don't have an explicit family — most page styles override this anyway, so the visible diff is at most a sub-pixel weight shift on plain text. Acceptable for A1's "no visual regression" bar; we will verify against the running dev server in a brief check before/after the next page-level commit (B1+) to catch any unexpected diff early.
- Issues: None. The pre-existing Element Plus full-import main-chunk >500 kB warning persists (out of scope, recorded since Tasks 5-9). The decision to defer the "minimal EP override" from A1 to the end of Phase B is documented in docs/phase1-ui-redesign.md §8 and again here so a future maintainer doesn't reintroduce A1-era EP overrides.

After A2 the global look starts to shift; A3 then introduces the atom components (Button, Pill, DotStatus, etc.) and A4 introduces ProductCover, before Phase B page-by-page slices. Each step still gates on user confirmation per [[feedback-phase1-frontend-workflow]] and [[feedback-commit-authorization]].

## Phase 1 UI rework — A2 AppShell
- Date: 2026-05-24
- Status: Done
- Branch: feature/phase1-customer-frontend
- TaskMaster tag: phase1-customer-frontend (no TaskMaster ID — UI rework continues under docs/phase1-ui-redesign.md, Phase 1 was already 10/10 before this effort started)
- Scope: Second step of the Phase 1 customer frontend visual/UX rework. Replaces the global shell (header + footer + page-transition wrapper) so the storefront identity becomes visible application-wide. This is the first commit in the rework where end-users will perceive a visual change — the body's --canvas (#F7F6F2 warm paper) now shines through, the header switches from the EP-default 60px white bar with #2563eb brand to a 72px-transparent / 56px-blurred two-state shell with a 6px terracotta dot beside a tracking-widened wordmark, and route changes animate via a brief fade + 8px translateY entrance.
- Implemented:
  - NEW frontend/src/components/BrandMark.vue (~50 lines) — accepts size ('sm' | 'md', default 'md') and dot (boolean) props. Renders an inline-flex span with an optional 6px terracotta dot and the "MiniMall" wordmark in --font-display (Inter Tight 600) at --t-brand-size (18px) with --t-brand-track (+0.04em letter-spacing); the sm variant drops the wordmark to 14px and the dot to 5px. Used by AppHeader (md + dot) and AppFooter (sm + no dot) so brand voice stays consistent across the top and bottom of every page.
  - NEW frontend/src/components/AppFooter.vue (~50 lines) — 80px-tall footer at canvas color with a top hairline (border-top: 1px solid var(--ink-100)). Inside the 1280px max-width inner row: BrandMark size="sm" on the left, "© {currentYear} MiniMall · 演示项目" caption on the right. The year is computed at component setup so it auto-rolls over. On <640px the inner padding shrinks to 16px. No business links, no policy footer columns — the brief explicitly forbids inventing features just to fill chrome.
  - REWRITE frontend/src/components/AppHeader.vue (78 → 493 lines) — replaces the Element Plus driven header with a custom scroll-aware shell per docs/phase1-ui-redesign.md §5.1.
    - Default state: 72px tall, transparent background, no border, sits at z-index 50 as position:sticky on the page so it floats over content while remaining click-target on scroll.
    - Scrolled state (window.scrollY > 8): inner row collapses to 56px, background fades to rgba(247,246,242,.85) with backdrop-filter: blur(8px) (-webkit- prefix included), border-bottom: 1px solid var(--ink-100). All three transitions cross-fade over --dur-2 (220ms) using --ease.
    - Layout: CSS grid (auto 1fr auto). Left cell: a RouterLink to /products wrapping <BrandMark :dot="true" />. Center cell: nav (logged-in only) holding two RouterLinks rendered as nav-pills ("Shop" → /products, "My Orders" → /orders). Each pill has padding 8/14, 999 radius, hover bg --ink-100. The .router-link-active state lifts color to --ink-900 and renders a 4×4 terracotta dot 8px below the pill via a ::after pseudo. Both pills receive a manually-forced router-link-active class via :class binding to cover sibling-route activation (see decisions below): isInProductsSection covers `/`, `/products`, `/products/:productId`, and `/checkout`; isInOrdersSection covers `/orders`, `/orders/:orderNo`, and `/payments/:orderNo`. When logged out, the nav is replaced by an empty span placeholder so the grid layout stays stable.
    - Right cell, logged-in: a 32px circular "account chip" (background --canvas-darker, hover --ink-100) showing the user's first initial in Inter Tight 600. Click opens a custom popover (NOT el-popover) — absolute positioned 12px below the chip, 200px min-width, surface white, 12px radius, shadow-2, holding: a username row (caption ink-500, ellipsis on overflow) above a hairline divider, then a full-width "Sign out" menuitem that hover-lifts to --ink-100. Popover is wrapped in <Transition name="popover"> with the same opacity + 4px translateY -4 → 0 motion as the mobile sheet, transitions --dur-2 220ms. Popover closes on: (1) document mousedown outside the chip/popover region (via a data-account-popover-root attribute selector so future class refactors can't break the test), (2) Escape keydown, (3) route change.
    - Right cell, logged-out: a plain "Sign in" text button (color --ink-700, hover --ink-900) and a "Create account" ghost button with --ink-300 border + 10px radius (hover border --ink-900 + bg --ink-100).
    - Mobile (<640px): center nav and account chip both display:none, replaced by a small hamburger menu-btn (two-bar 18×1.5px ink-900 lines). Click toggles a <Transition name="sheet"> slide-down panel (absolute, top:100%, top+bottom hairlines, shadow-1) containing: Shop link, My Orders link (also driven by isInOrdersSection), divider, username caption, and a Sign out button. Each link's @click also closes the sheet. The sheet only renders when both sheetOpen && auth.isLoggedIn; unauthenticated mobile users keep the inline Sign in / Create account buttons in the right cell (they fit at 320px width).
    - Event lifecycle: onMounted attaches passive scroll listener + document mousedown listener + keydown listener (Escape). onBeforeUnmount removes all three. A watch on route.fullPath collapses both popoverOpen and sheetOpen on every navigation so transient UI never persists across pages.
  - MODIFIED frontend/src/layouts/DefaultLayout.vue (26 → 52 lines) — adds the footer slot, wraps router-view in <Transition name="page" mode="out-in">, and removes the previous `background: #f5f6f8` so the body's --canvas now reaches the viewport. The transition is configured per brief §5.1 + §7: outgoing leave is opacity-only over --dur-1 (120ms), incoming enter is opacity + translateY 8 → 0 over --dur-2 (220ms); the asymmetric durations mean the perceived total page-change time is ~340ms (120 out + 220 in via mode="out-in"), giving routes a subtle "settle" rhythm without feeling slow. The layout switches to a column flex (header / main flex:1 / footer) so the footer sits at the viewport bottom on short pages. Outer max-width on main is now 1280px (up from 1200px) to match the product list spec; individual views remain free to self-constrain to narrower widths (Checkout 720 actual / Payment 720 actual today; Phase B will trim these to 560 / 480 per the brief).
- Decisions and trade-offs:
  - Custom popover and sheet, NOT el-popover / el-drawer. Per docs/phase1-ui-redesign.md §3.1, customer-visible chrome must replace EP. The Sign-out popover is the smallest such replacement and serves as a template: positioning is absolute relative to the chip's positioned container, click-outside uses a single document mousedown listener filtered by a data-* attribute (no Vue refs needed), Escape is handled by a single document keydown listener. The same pattern carries forward to the eventual <PaymentMethodCard> and future popovers.
  - Page transition uses Vue's <Transition mode="out-in"> instead of overlapping enter/leave. The brief specifies 120ms out + 220ms in; with mode="out-in" the user sees a brief blank moment between routes, but it stays under 350ms wall-clock and prevents the two views from layering during the cross-fade (which causes scroll-position flicker and double-mounted children).
  - Active-section detection works symmetrically through two explicit computeds — isInProductsSection (`/`, `/products`, `/products/:productId`, `/checkout`) and isInOrdersSection (`/orders`, `/orders/:orderNo`, `/payments/:orderNo`) — both bound to the corresponding pill's router-link-active class via :class. The reason this is necessary at all: router/index.ts registers `/products` + `/products/:productId` and `/orders` + `/orders/:orderNo` as PARALLEL routes, not as nested children. Vue Router 4's automatic .router-link-active matching walks the matched route's record chain (parent links) — it does NOT pure-string-prefix match — so sibling routes never inherit each other's active state. A live verification of this surfaced the bug mid-A2 review (the user navigated to `/products/:productId` and noticed Shop didn't highlight); the symmetric isInProductsSection was added immediately so both navigational concepts behave identically. Touching router/index.ts to introduce nesting was considered and rejected — it would have been less code but is forbidden under R9 (§10) of the design contract, which keeps src/router/ off-limits during the UI rework so each commit's risk surface stays purely visual.
  - The header is position:sticky so it stays visible as the user scrolls a product list or order list; the alternative (position:relative) would make the brand vanish after the first viewport, which is a worse storefront feel. Sticky on the header also establishes the containing block for the absolute-positioned mobile sheet — convenient because it anchors the sheet directly below the header regardless of the header's collapsed/expanded height.
  - Mobile chip + popover are completely hidden on <640px in favor of the menu button + sheet. Showing both at small widths would crowd the header and double up the sign-out affordance.
  - DefaultLayout's outer main bumped from 1200 → 1280 to fit the product list spec. All currently-shipped views self-constrain (Checkout/Payment at 720, Orders details at 720, etc.), so widening the outer container only relaxes the product list grid; nothing actually shrinks or shifts on existing pages aside from product list cards getting marginally more breathing room. Phase B will further tighten the per-page widths via the upcoming <PageContainer> atom (A3).
- Changed files: frontend/src/components/BrandMark.vue (NEW); frontend/src/components/AppFooter.vue (NEW); frontend/src/components/AppHeader.vue (rewrite, 78 → 493 lines); frontend/src/layouts/DefaultLayout.vue (modified, 26 → 52 lines); docs/dev-log.md (this entry).
- Commands run: `git status` + `git branch --show-current` + `git log --oneline -1` at start (clean, on feature/phase1-customer-frontend, last commit c981014 A1); cd frontend && `npm run build` (vue-tsc --noEmit + vite build, exit 0, 3.56s wall-clock; rebuilt after the isInProductsSection fix, exit 0, 4.31s); `npx vitest run` (9/9 pass, ~0.87s before fix, ~1.13s after); `git status --short` + `git diff --stat` to confirm staged set is exactly the 4 expected files. Backend brought up via `docker compose --env-file .env --profile services up -d` (12 containers all healthy, gateway probe `curl :8080/actuator/health` returned `{"status":"UP"}`, canonical endpoint `:8080/api/inventories/PHASE0-SMOKE-20260521` returned the seeded 45+5=50 inventory snapshot intact from the persisted MySQL volume) so the user could run the live verification that surfaced the sibling-route active-state bug.
- Test result: npm run build clean. Build deltas vs A1 (commit c981014): index CSS 363.12 → 369.34 kB (+6.22 kB, the new AppHeader/AppFooter/DefaultLayout scoped styles); main JS bundle 1082.99 → 1086.38 kB (+3.39 kB, the new header script — scroll listener, popover/sheet state, computed, watch). All lazy-loaded view chunks stayed byte-identical to A1 (PaymentView 9.27 kB, CheckoutView 6.64 kB, ProductDetailView 5.87 kB, OrderDetailView 5.41 kB, OrdersView 4.57 kB, ProductListView 3.69 kB, RegisterView 3.55 kB, LoginView 2.31 kB) — confirming no view code was touched. Vitest: 9/9 pass in ~0.87s wall-clock. No type errors. The pre-existing Element Plus full-import >500 kB warning persists (out of scope, recorded since Tasks 5-9).
- Visual smoke: Not run live against the dev server in this commit's tool calls (Bash cannot drive a real browser); the user should run `npm run dev` and walk through the expected post-A2 effects: (1) every page now sits on the warm --canvas (#F7F6F2) background instead of #f5f6f8; (2) header default is 72px transparent with terracotta dot + wordmark; on scroll>8px it collapses to 56px with backdrop blur and a hairline; (3) on /products the "Shop" pill shows a 4px terracotta dot below it; visiting /orders/:orderNo or /payments/:orderNo highlights "My Orders" instead (the .router-link-active manual mapping); (4) clicking the account chip opens a small popover showing the username + a Sign out menuitem; clicking outside, pressing Escape, or navigating away all close it; (5) signed-out pages show "Sign in" + "Create account" in the top-right instead of the chip; (6) every route change cross-fades over ~340ms with the incoming view sliding up 8px; (7) the footer appears at the bottom with the small wordmark + copyright caption; (8) at viewport widths <640px the center nav and chip collapse, a hamburger menu-btn appears, and clicking it slides down a sheet with the same links + sign-out. Existing purchase loop should still work (no view code touched, no router changes, no API touches).
- Issues: None known. The header's backdrop-filter requires browser support; Safari 15+ / Chrome 76+ / Firefox 103+ all support it, fallback browsers will see a flat semi-transparent canvas color without blur (acceptable visual degradation, never breaks layout). The sheet's slide-down animation uses transform + opacity; no layout reflow. The mobile sheet currently does not implement a body scroll lock, so a user can scroll the page underneath while the sheet is open; given the sheet is small (≤5 rows) and dismisses on any link tap, scroll lock would be over-engineering — added to mental backlog only if a real complaint surfaces. The mobile menu-btn intentionally does not animate the bars into an X on open (one less CSS bit to maintain); the aria-expanded attribute toggles correctly for screen readers regardless. Two-bar hamburger over the conventional three-bar is the brief's choice per §5.1 ("a 'Menu' button"); both are common conventions.
- Next: A3 — atom components (Button, Pill, DotStatus, PriceText, Hairline, Field, QuantityStepper, Skeleton, SkeletonText, Notice, Pager, PillGroup). These do not change any page yet; they just become available for Phase B page-by-page slices to consume. A4 follows with ProductCover (the determinism-tested no-backend product visual system). Then Phase B begins with B1 (product list rewrite).

## Phase 1 UI rework — A3 Atom components
- Date: 2026-05-24
- Status: Done
- Branch: feature/phase1-customer-frontend
- TaskMaster tag: phase1-customer-frontend (no TaskMaster ID — UI rework continues under docs/phase1-ui-redesign.md)
- Scope: Third step of the Phase 1 customer frontend UI rework. Introduces the storefront design-system atom library — 12 small, pure-presentation Vue components plus one Vitest spec — without touching any view, layout, router, store, api, types, util, or backend file. Because no view imports any of these yet, A3 produces ZERO visual change on every customer-facing page; the atoms only become consumed during Phase B's page-by-page slices (B1+). The point of shipping them as a single foundational commit is so that B1, B2, etc. can each focus on view layout and consume a stable, already-shipped vocabulary, rather than re-litigating button shape, pill tone, and skeleton motion mid-page.
- Implemented:
  - NEW frontend/src/components/atoms/Button.vue (~165 lines) — three variants (primary = ink-900 filled, ghost = ink-300 outline, text = no chrome) × three sizes (sm 32h / md 40h / lg 48h). Loading state replaces label with three 1.2s ease-in-out staggered pulse dots (animation-delay 0/0.15/0.30s) and forces aria-busy=true + disabled=true so a click cannot fire. Press-state visual is scale(0.98) over --dur-1 120ms via :active:not(:disabled). full prop spans 100% width. Default type="button" (prevents accidental form submission); callers pass type="submit" explicitly when needed. prefers-reduced-motion blocks the scale, transition, and dot pulse. The variant + size + state combination matrix is the single source of truth for every storefront CTA; AppHeader's existing inline .signin-link / .ghost-btn / popover .account__signout are NOT migrated in this commit — that's a Phase D polish task, not a Phase B risk.
  - NEW frontend/src/components/atoms/Pill.vue (~95 lines) — `<Pill tone="neutral|terracotta|success|warn|danger" :soft>` defaults to soft (light tone background + same-hue text, no border) because storefront usage is exclusively soft. Solid variant kept for completeness (full-saturation background + white text) but unused in Phase 1. Used as the eventual replacement for el-tag across product cards, order cards, status overlays.
  - NEW frontend/src/components/atoms/DotStatus.vue (~85 lines) — `<DotStatus tone="..." label="..." :pulse>` renders a 7×7 colored dot + label inline. tone maps to the five color tokens (ink-500 neutral / terracotta / success green / warn amber / danger red). Optional pulse adds a 1.2s ease-in-out scale 1↔1.25 + opacity 1↔0.7 breathing animation, used in §5.7 for the pending-payment order card's status row. prefers-reduced-motion disables the pulse. Accepts either a `label` prop or a default slot for the text — the slot wins when both are present (Vue's default slot fallback behavior).
  - NEW frontend/src/components/atoms/PriceText.vue (~75 lines) — `<PriceText :amount="123.45" size="sm|md|lg|xl">` with a fixed-2-decimal toFixed formatter. Default size md (20px/600). lg (32px/700) maps to product detail price; xl (56px/700) uses --font-display + -0.01em letter-spacing and maps to payment-page amount block. All sizes set font-variant-numeric: tabular-nums so prices stack cleanly in vertical lists (order summary, checkout totals). Currency prop defaults to ¥ but accepts any short string; non-finite amounts collapse to 0.00 silently rather than rendering "NaN".
  - NEW frontend/src/components/atoms/Hairline.vue (~50 lines) — `<Hairline :vertical :inset />` renders a 1px var(--ink-100) divider. Horizontal default is a semantic `<hr>` (height 1px, width 100%); vertical mode renders a `<span role="separator" aria-orientation="vertical">` 1px wide × 1em tall, suitable for inline meta-row separators. inset modifier adds 16px horizontal margin so the line sits inside a card's padding box rather than spanning full width.
  - NEW frontend/src/components/atoms/Field.vue (~65 lines) — `<Field label hint error>` form-field shell. Renders label (13/500 ink-700) above a slot (consumer drops their `<el-input>` or any other input into the slot), then a single helper paragraph below. When `error` is set, the helper switches to danger tone + replaces the hint. The slot deliberately does NOT wrap el-form-item — el-form's validation engine stays in the consuming view (B7 login/register), Field just provides the visible shell so the input doesn't carry el-form-item's default chrome.
  - NEW frontend/src/components/atoms/QuantityStepper.vue (~145 lines) — `<QuantityStepper v-model="qty" :min="1" :max="999" :step="1" :disabled>` replaces el-input-number. Layout: [−] [native number input] [+] inside an ink-300-bordered, 10px-radius, 40px-tall container. Each step button is 40px square with hover ink-100 + active ink-300; the native input is centered, 56px wide, tabular-nums, with -webkit-/-moz- spin-button suppression so no native arrows show. The component owns its clamp logic — clamp(n) = max(min, min(max, floor(n))) — applied at three touch points: (1) increment / decrement, both of which also check the canDec/canInc computed and emit nothing if at the boundary so the v-model never receives a no-op update; (2) onInput, which silently skips empty strings (so the user can transiently clear the field during typing) but clamps non-empty integer-parseable values; (3) onBlur, which finalizes the input — empty or non-integer values snap to min, otherwise clamp. The disabled prop short-circuits canDec/canInc to false, fades the surface, and disables the native input — three layers of belt-and-suspenders so a disabled stepper cannot emit anything. Integer-only is the contract because the view layer treats quantity as a unit count.
  - NEW frontend/src/components/atoms/Skeleton.vue (~75 lines) — `<Skeleton :width :height :radius :block>` renders a single shimmering placeholder. Background is a 200%-wide linear-gradient(90deg, ink-100, canvas-darker, ink-100) animated 1.6s ease-in-out infinite via background-position 200% → -200%.
