Default 100% width × 16px height, sm radius. radius prop accepts sm | md | lg | xl | full. block prop switches display:inline-block → display:block so the skeleton can size to its parent column without trailing-whitespace issues. prefers-reduced-motion replaces the gradient sweep with a static ink-100 fill (so the structure still communicates "this slot is loading" without motion).
  - NEW frontend/src/components/atoms/SkeletonText.vue (~50 lines) — `<SkeletonText :lines="3" :lineHeight="12px" :gap="10px">` stacks Skeleton atoms vertically. The last line is 60% wide when lines > 1, giving a natural ragged-right paragraph feel; with lines=1 the single line is 100% (no fake-paragraph illusion). Used inside product list / order list skeleton compositions in Phase B.
  - NEW frontend/src/components/atoms/Notice.vue (~75 lines) — `<Notice tone="info|warn|danger|neutral" title>` replaces el-alert. Hairline-bordered card (no harsh fill except a soft tone-tinted background for warn/danger) with title (13/600) optional + default slot for body content (13/400 ink-700). Title is colored by tone (warn → --warn, danger → --danger). neutral tone uses canvas-darker background — used in §5.9 for the payment page's "Demo payment" disclosure chip.
  - NEW frontend/src/components/atoms/Pager.vue (~135 lines) — `<Pager :total :pageSize :current @change>`. Computed pageCount = max(1, ceil(total/pageSize)). pages: when pageCount ≤ 7 lists every page; when > 7 collapses to [1, '…', current-1, current, current+1, '…', last], always preserving first and last. Layout: "← Previous" text-link button on the left, numbered page chips in the middle (32px square, current-page in ink-900 filled white, others ink-500 with ink-100 hover), "Next →" on the right. Prev/Next disable at boundaries. Whole `<nav>` is hidden via v-if when pageCount === 1 (no degenerate single-page UI). Emits change(page) — the parent owns currentPage state and is responsible for re-fetching.
  - NEW frontend/src/components/atoms/PillGroup.vue (~75 lines) — `<PillGroup :options="[{value, label}]" v-model="selected">` renders a horizontal `<div role="tablist">` of pill toggles. Active pill is ink-900 filled white (cursor:default since clicking the active option is a no-op); inactive pills are ink-300 outlined and hover-fill ink-100 + darken to ink-900. Used as the filter row on product list (全部 / 在售 / 已下架) and the orders list status tab (全部 / 待支付 / 已支付 / 已取消). Generic value: string contract — the consuming view interprets the value strings as needed (status enum, query string, etc.).
  - NEW frontend/src/components/__tests__/QuantityStepper.spec.ts (~80 lines, 7 tests) — covers the QuantityStepper contract since it carries the only real behavior in this commit's atom set: (1) + click emits clamp(modelValue+step); (2) − click emits clamp(modelValue-step); (3) at modelValue=max the + button is disabled AND a programmatic click emits nothing; (4) symmetric for min on −; (5) typed value above max emits clamp result (max), not the raw value; (6) clearing the input and blurring snaps to min; (7) disabled=true disables both step buttons and the native input. Uses enableAutoUnmount(afterEach) like the existing PaymentView/CheckoutView specs so cross-test wrapper bleed cannot happen.
- Decisions and trade-offs:
  - Atoms live under components/atoms/ in a subdirectory so they're visually grouped and separated from molecules (AppHeader, AppFooter, BrandMark) and from views. The subdir is "library" — these files have no business state, no api dependency, no router/store touch. Phase B's molecules (ProductCard, OrderCard, AmountDisplay, etc.) will sit at components/ root level alongside AppHeader, importing from atoms/.
  - QuantityStepper picked native `<input type="number">` as the core, NOT a custom contenteditable. Native input gives: real keyboard handling (arrow keys, mobile numeric keypad via inputmode="numeric"), real :disabled propagation, accessibility name via aria-label. We accept the cost of suppressing the native spin buttons via -webkit-/-moz- pseudo-elements because the +/− buttons are the storefront's preferred affordance.
  - Pill's soft=true is the default because every storefront usage in §5 is soft; the solid variant exists for future "promo banner" scenarios but is unused in Phase 1. Keeps the call sites terse: `<Pill tone="success">在售</Pill>` is the common case.
  - Notice and Pill differ deliberately: Pill is a tiny status chip (22px tall, no border, single label), Notice is a multi-line tone-tinted card (with title + slot body). They're not interchangeable; el-tag → Pill, el-alert → Notice.
  - Skeleton/SkeletonText don't include role="status" or aria-live — they're aria-hidden so screen readers don't announce "loading loading loading" repeatedly while the shimmer cycles. The view-level loading state should expose a single accessible loading message (the consuming view's responsibility, not the atom's).
  - Pager truncation kicks in at pageCount > 7, which matches the typical e-commerce list size (10 items per page × 7+ pages = 70+ items). For Phase 1 demo seed data we'll usually see 1-3 pages so the v-if hides the whole nav at pageCount=1.
  - Field deliberately does NOT host the validation logic. el-form + el-form-item still own that; Field is purely the visible shell. This way B7 login/register can keep the existing rules + form.validate() flow unchanged — only the visible chrome swaps.
  - No design-probe / Storybook route was added for visual sanity-checking the atoms in isolation. The trade-off is that the next time we touch one of these we'll need to spin up a quick consuming view, but adding a probe page brings non-trivial routing + lazy-chunk overhead that isn't worth it for a 12-component set whose first real consumer (ProductCard) ships in B1.
  - prefers-reduced-motion is honored in Button, DotStatus, and Skeleton — the three atoms with non-decorative animation. Pill, PillGroup, Pager, Notice, Hairline, PriceText, Field, SkeletonText have no animation to honor.
- Changed files: 12 new atom Vue files under frontend/src/components/atoms/; 1 new spec file frontend/src/components/__tests__/QuantityStepper.spec.ts; docs/dev-log.md (this entry). Zero modifications to existing files.
- Commands run: `git status` + `git branch --show-current` + `git log --oneline -2` at start (clean, last commits e5e593d A2 / c981014 A1); cd frontend && `npm run build` (vue-tsc --noEmit + vite build, exit 0, 3.97s wall-clock); `npx vitest run` (3 spec files / 16 tests pass, ~1.07s — PaymentView 4 + CheckoutView 5 from Phase 1 follow-up b1e5768 + QuantityStepper 7 new); `git status --short` + `git diff --stat` + `git ls-files --others --exclude-standard` to confirm staged set is exactly the 14 new files (12 atoms + 1 spec + dev-log) and that no existing file was modified.
- Test result: npm run build clean. Build deltas vs A2 (commit e5e593d): main bundle index-T-gHTfFy.js 1086.38 → 1086.56 kB (+0.18 kB — atoms are unused so tree-shaking removed nearly all of them; the tiny residual is shared utility shape that the optimizer kept); ALL lazy-loaded view chunks stayed byte-identical to A2 (PaymentView 9.27, CheckoutView 6.64, ProductDetailView 5.87, OrderDetailView 5.41, OrdersView 4.57, ProductListView 3.69, RegisterView 3.55, LoginView 2.31 kB) confirming zero view code was touched. Index CSS likewise unchanged at 369.34 kB since no atom CSS gets bundled until a view imports the atom. Vitest 16/16 pass (was 9/9 before A3) in ~1.07s — the 7 new QuantityStepper tests passed first run, no flakes. No type errors. The pre-existing Element Plus full-import >500 kB warning persists (out of scope, recorded since Tasks 5-9).
- Visual smoke: Intentionally not exercised in this commit because A3 introduces NO consumer of the new atoms — every customer-facing page still renders identically to the post-A2 state (canvas color, scroll-aware header, page transition, footer, EP-default product cards / order cards / etc.). The atoms will get their first live visual validation in B1 (product list rewrite) when ProductCard consumes ProductCover (A4) + Pill + DotStatus + PriceText + Skeleton.
- Issues: None known. The atoms are intentionally scope-limited to "what Phase B will consume" — not a general-purpose design system. If a Phase B page surfaces a need for a new atom (e.g. a SelectField for some future filter), that atom will get added at that step. The pre-existing >500 kB Element Plus warning persists, unchanged.
- Next: A4 — ProductCover system. Pure-frontend deterministic product visual: fnv1a(productId) → palette + geometry + initial mark; rendered at 4:5 in list cards, 4:5 detail-grade in product hero (with extra layers + noise overlay), 1:1 in order/checkout rows. Includes a small utils/cover.ts with hash + palette/geometry selection (unit-testable) and a Vitest spec confirming determinism (same productId → same output). After A4 lands, A5 introduces EmptyState + ErrorState. Then Phase B begins with B1 (product list rewrite — the first commit where customer-facing visuals start changing per page).

## Phase 1 UI rework — A4 ProductCover system
- Date: 2026-05-24
- Status: Done
- Branch: feature/phase1-customer-frontend
- TaskMaster tag: phase1-customer-frontend (no TaskMaster ID — UI rework continues under docs/phase1-ui-redesign.md)
- Scope: Fourth step of the Phase 1 customer frontend UI rework. Ships the programmatic product-cover system — a pure-function spec resolver (utils/cover.ts), a thin SVG renderer (components/ProductCover.vue), and a Vitest spec covering determinism + edge cases. The backend product API does not return any image URL, and we are forbidden from changing it, so every product visual in the storefront has to be generated client-side. The contract is: given a productId (and optionally a name), the resolver returns a fully-deterministic CoverSpec — same inputs ALWAYS produce the same palette, geometry, rotation, offset, and initial mark — so the same product looks identical on the list card, the detail hero, the order row, and the checkout summary. No view imports ProductCover yet (B1 will be the first consumer), so this commit produces ZERO visual change on every customer-facing page.
- Implemented:
  - NEW frontend/src/utils/cover.ts (~115 lines) — three exports: fnv1a(str) returns a 32-bit unsigned FNV-1a hash via Math.imul (10 lines, no deps); extractInitial(name) walks the trimmed string char-by-char with a CJK Unified Ideographs (main + Extension A) + CJK Compatibility Ideographs regex and returns the first CJK glyph it finds, falling back to up to 2 alphanumeric chars uppercased after stripping non-alphanumerics, and falling back to '?' for empty/whitespace/non-alphanumeric input; coverFor(productId, name) hashes `${productId}::${name}` and uses different bit-ranges of the hash to pick palette (hash % 8), geometry (hash>>>8 % 6), rotation in 15° steps (hash>>>16 % 24 × 15), and two small offsets in [-0.2, 0.2] (different 8-bit windows mapped through (b/255 - 0.5) × 0.4). The seed itself is exposed on the returned spec so the SVG renderer can build stable `<defs>` ids without an instance counter — same product → same gradient id → no DOM duplication noise.
  - NEW frontend/src/components/ProductCover.vue (~210 lines) — `<ProductCover :productId :name :aspect :grade :size />`. Computes the spec via coverFor, then renders an inline SVG with three layers: (1) a vertical linearGradient base (palette.base → palette.baseDark); (2) a single geometry primitive rendered inside `<g transform="rotate(θ cx cy)">` where the primitive type is determined by spec.geometry — disc (large circle, 0.36 × major axis radius), arc (half-circle path from -0.42 to +0.42), lines (3 horizontal rectangles at y offsets -0.18 / -0.02 / +0.14), rings (3 concentric stroke-only circles at radii 0.4 / 0.28 / 0.16), diamond (rotated 56% × 56% square, additional rotate(45) on top of the spec rotation), composite (a triangle + a small filled circle in accentDeep); (3) a bottom-left initial mark in Inter Tight 700 at 18% of viewBox height, accentDeep color, 0.92 opacity. When grade='detail' two extra layers stack on top: a radial halo gradient at the top-right (accent at 0.2 opacity fading to 0% over 60% radius) and an feTurbulence fractalNoise filter at 0.05 alpha matrix giving the cover detail-grade tactile texture for the product detail hero. The figure element gets its dimensions from a size prop (sm 64 / md 160 / lg 280 / full 100%) combined with a CSS aspect-ratio derived from aspect (4:5 / 1:1 / 16:9), so the cover always preserves its proportion regardless of container width. preserveAspectRatio="xMidYMid slice" + the explicit aspect-ratio together prevent any letterboxing.
  - NEW frontend/src/utils/__tests__/cover.spec.ts (~110 lines, 17 tests across 3 describe blocks) — fnv1a: determinism for the same input including a CJK example, distinct-output for different inputs, range check (unsigned 32-bit integer) over 5 sample strings; extractInitial: first CJK glyph including mid-string CJK ("Premium 茶具 set" → "茶"), Latin uppercased slice (aroma → AR, a → A), non-alphanumeric stripped before slicing (3-pack → 3P, !!premium → PR), all four nullish/empty fallbacks return '?'; coverFor: deterministic same-input round-trip including a CJK product name, numeric and string productId yield identical spec (so the caller doesn't need to .toString()), 100-sample sweeps confirm palette ∈ PALETTES and geometry ∈ GEOMETRIES, rotation is always a multiple of 15 in [0, 360), offsets always within [-0.2, 0.2], null/undefined/empty inputs don't throw, different productIds OR different names yield distinct seeds, initial wiring (CJK → first glyph, latin → 2 uppercased, empty → '?').
  - APPENDED docs/dev-log.md (this entry).
- Decisions and trade-offs:
  - FNV-1a was picked over djb2 or a CRC variant because it's (a) trivial to write in 10 lines without lookup tables, (b) produces good distribution across the 8-palette × 6-geometry × 24-rotation × 256-offset space we actually use, and (c) is stable across Node, browsers, and any future SSR runtime. We don't need cryptographic strength here — just stable per-product visual identity.
  - The hash input is `${idStr}::${nameStr}` rather than just `${idStr}` so that two products with the same numeric id but different names (which shouldn't happen in production but could in test fixtures) get distinct visuals. The `::` separator prevents ambiguity between e.g. (id="1", name="2A") and (id="12", name="A"). The name still primarily feeds the initial mark; its contribution to the hash is incidental.
  - The 6 geometries are intentionally abstract — no realistic product silhouettes (no candle shapes, no bottle outlines, etc.). The brief calls for a boutique-magazine feel, not an icon library. Customers immediately learn that the cover is a stylized visual signature for the product, not a photo, which sidesteps the entire "this looks like a placeholder" failure mode that fake product icons would create.
  - The initial mark sits at the bottom-left (0.08 × w, 0.92 × h) rather than centered, because a centered mark fights with the geometry layer for focal weight; the corner placement reads as a signed-print maker's mark and lets the geometry breathe. accentDeep was chosen over accent for the text fill because the deeper shade reads more clearly over the lighter geometry shapes when they happen to overlap the text area.
  - Detail-grade is opt-in via grade='detail', not derived from size or aspect. The cost is a turbulence filter (which is GPU-rasterized but non-trivial) plus an extra radial gradient. We only want to pay that cost on the product detail hero, not on a 30-card list view or a 32px order-row thumbnail — even though all three use the same component.
  - SVG ids are derived from spec.seed (e.g. `pcv-grad-${seed}`). Two ProductCover instances of the same product on the same page will produce identical id strings — that's intentional and correct, because the referenced `<linearGradient>` definitions are literally the same definition. SVG `url(#id)` reference resolves to the first matching element in the document, which works fine in this case. Different products will produce different ids because their seeds differ.
  - Component lives at components/ root level (NOT components/atoms/) because it's a molecule, not an atom — it composes the cover spec with SVG geometry logic and grade-conditional layers. The atom subfolder is reserved for pure-presentation primitives (Button, Pill, Skeleton, etc.) with no business logic. ProductCover's coverFor call qualifies as light business logic (deterministic visual identity per product), so it belongs at the molecule level alongside future ProductCard, OrderCard, etc.
  - No Vitest tests for the ProductCover.vue render output itself were added. The render is purely a function of the CoverSpec (which IS tested), and DOM-snapshot tests for SVG are brittle (whitespace, attribute order). The visual contract gets validated by the consuming-view tests in Phase B (e.g. B1's ProductCard.spec) and by manual visual smoke once a view actually mounts it.
- Changed files: NEW frontend/src/utils/cover.ts; NEW frontend/src/components/ProductCover.vue; NEW frontend/src/utils/__tests__/cover.spec.ts; docs/dev-log.md (this entry). Zero modifications to existing files.
- Commands run: `git status` + `git log --oneline -5` at start (clean, HEAD c13a2db A3); `ls frontend/src/utils/` + `ls frontend/src/components/atoms/` + `ls frontend/src/components/__tests__/` to confirm file locations; `cat frontend/vite.config.ts` to confirm the vitest include glob picks up `src/**/*.{test,spec}.ts` (so src/utils/__tests__/cover.spec.ts auto-discovers); `mkdir -p frontend/src/utils/__tests__`; `npx vitest run` (4 spec files / 33 tests pass, ~1.05s — PaymentView 4 + CheckoutView 5 + QuantityStepper 7 + cover 17 new); `npm run build` (vue-tsc --noEmit + vite build, exit 0, 3.86s); chunk-size diff vs A3 (c13a2db) verified — main bundle and every view chunk byte-identical.
- Test result: 33/33 vitest tests pass (was 16/16 before A4; +17 from cover.spec.ts) in ~1.05s, no flakes — including the determinism round-trip, the 100-sample palette/geometry/rotation/offset sweeps, the numeric-vs-string id equivalence, and the empty/null edge cases. `npm run build` clean. Build deltas vs A3 (commit c13a2db): main bundle index-T-gHTfFy.js stayed BYTE-IDENTICAL at 1086.56 kB (utils/cover.ts is a small pure-function module and ProductCover.vue is a single-file component; both are fully tree-shaken because no view imports them yet); ALL 8 lazy view chunks byte-identical (LoginView 2.31, RegisterView 3.55, ProductListView 3.69, OrdersView 4.57, OrderDetailView 5.41, ProductDetailView 5.87, CheckoutView 6.64, PaymentView 9.27 kB); index CSS unchanged at 369.34 kB. No type errors. The pre-existing Element Plus full-import >500 kB warning persists (out of scope, recorded since Tasks 5-9).
- Visual smoke: Intentionally not exercised — A4 introduces no consumer. Every customer-facing page still renders identically to post-A3 state (post-A2 visuals, since A3 also added no consumers). ProductCover gets its first live validation in B1 (product list rewrite) where ProductCard consumes it at aspect='4:5' grade='list', then again in B2 (product detail) at aspect='4:5' grade='detail', then B3 (checkout) and B5 (order detail) at aspect='1:1' size='sm'.
- Issues: None known. The 6-geometry × 8-palette × 24-rotation matrix gives 1,152 distinct base appearances before offsets — more than enough for the small-double-digit product catalog the Phase 0 seed data ships with. If a future product catalog grows past a few thousand unique products and customers start noticing visual collisions, the next lever is to expand the geometry set or add an additional hue-shift parameter; both are non-breaking additions to cover.ts. The pre-existing >500 kB Element Plus warning persists, unchanged.
- Next: A5 — EmptyState + ErrorState components. Two small slot-driven components that replace the current `<el-empty>` and `<el-result>` chrome with the brief's storefront aesthetic — soft hairline-bordered cards, terracotta accent on the suggested CTA, no harsh red error fills. After A5, Phase A is fully done and Phase B begins with B1 (product list rewrite — the first commit where customer-facing visuals start changing per page, and the first consumer of ProductCover + Pill + DotStatus + PriceText + Skeleton).

## Phase 1 UI rework — A5 EmptyState + ErrorState
- Date: 2026-05-24
- Status: Done
- Branch: feature/phase1-customer-frontend
- TaskMaster tag: phase1-customer-frontend (no TaskMaster ID — UI rework continues under docs/phase1-ui-redesign.md)
- Scope: Fifth and final step of Phase A. Ships two small molecule components — EmptyState and ErrorState — that will replace every `<el-empty>` and `<el-result>` instance in the storefront during Phase B. Both consume A3's Button atom; both are pure presentation with no api/store/router touch. No view imports either component yet, so this commit produces ZERO visual change on every customer-facing page. With A5 landing, Phase A (foundation infrastructure) is complete and Phase B (page-by-page rewrites) can begin.
- Implemented:
  - NEW frontend/src/components/EmptyState.vue (~95 lines) — `<EmptyState :title :description :showAction :actionLabel :actionDisabled @action>`. Renders a vertical stack centered on the page area: (1) a 120×120 inline SVG art block — a soft canvas-darker circle background with a thin ink-300 outlined inner circle (suggesting "an empty container") sitting above two ink-300 horizontal lines at decreasing opacity (suggesting "no items in a list"), all built from primitive shapes so the cost is ~12 lines of SVG and zero icon-library weight; (2) an h2 title (var(--t-h2-size) 18/600 ink-900 line-height 1.4); (3) an optional 13/400 ink-500 description capped at 360px max-width; (4) an optional primary Button at the bottom — gated by both showAction prop AND a non-empty actionLabel so the slot-area collapses cleanly when there's nothing to render. The component emits a single 'action' event (zero payload); the consuming view binds router push / re-fetch / whatever. The art deliberately avoids any literal interpretation (no shopping bag, no magnifying glass, no sad face) — it's the "neutral container with empty rows" abstraction that works the same for an empty product filter, an empty orders list, and any future empty surface.
  - NEW frontend/src/components/ErrorState.vue (~140 lines) — `<ErrorState :tone="'error'|'forbidden'|'notfound'" :title :description :showRetry :retryLabel :retryLoading :showHome :homeLabel @retry @home>`. Same overall structure as EmptyState — 120×120 art + title + optional description + optional CTA row — but the art switches per tone, and the CTA row can render two buttons side-by-side. Three tones with three distinct visual signatures: (1) `tone='error'` uses an accent-terracotta-soft circle background + a deliberately UNCLOSED accent-terracotta arc (270° sweep from the top-right corner, terminating with a small filled dot) — the unclosed arc reads as "interrupted" without ever drawing a literal warning triangle or red ×; (2) `tone='forbidden'` uses an ink-100 circle background + two offset 32×32 ink-500 stroke-only squares, the second offset by 10px diagonally and reduced to 0.6 opacity — abstract "two boundaries that don't align" metaphor for permission denied, no literal padlock icon; (3) `tone='notfound'` uses a canvas-darker background + a question-mark shape decomposed into a 14-radius ink-700 arc + a separate 3-radius filled dot, drawn from primitives rather than as a `<text>?</text>` glyph so it inherits the same stroke-weight + line-cap as the other tones' geometry. All three SVGs are 120×120, viewBox 0 0 120 120, no external icons, no filter primitives — they render identically to A4's ProductCover in their visual language (soft circle background + thin geometric primitive). CTA row hosts up to two Buttons: a primary 'Retry' (gated by showRetry, with retryLoading mapped through to Button's loading prop so the retry-in-flight state gets the dots animation) and a ghost 'Go home' (gated by showHome). Default retryLabel '重试' and homeLabel '返回首页'; consumers override if they want English or a different verb. The component emits 'retry' and 'home' — both zero-payload, the consuming view owns the actual action.
  - APPENDED docs/dev-log.md (this entry).
- Decisions and trade-offs:
  - Both components live at components/ root level (NOT components/atoms/) because they compose atoms (Button) and they encode page-level visual rhythm (the 64px vertical padding, the 16px gap between art / title / description / action, the 360px max-width on the description). Atoms are leaves; these are molecules.
  - No separate base "State" component to share the layout between Empty and Error. The two are 80% identical CSS but the per-tone art logic in ErrorState would force conditional rendering inside a shared shell — that ends up MORE code than just letting each component own its own shell. The duplication is ~30 lines of identical CSS and it's tolerable; if a third state component appears (LoadingState? PendingState?) we'll extract.
  - The error tone's "unclosed arc" art was tried first as a literal warning triangle and then as a circle-with-slash before settling on the unclosed arc — the arc is the only one that reads as "something happened" without reading as "Element Plus error icon". The terracotta-only palette (no danger red) is deliberate: per the brief §0 anti-patterns, harsh red fills are an admin-dashboard tell. The accent-terracotta is the storefront's single accent color, used everywhere errors are surfaced; it's not "soft" — it's the brand voice consistent with cancel buttons, the active nav dot, and the upcoming "Demo payment" disclosure chip.
  - The forbidden tone uses ink-only (no accent terracotta) because forbidden states are NOT errors in the user-recoverable sense — they're "you are not logged in" or "you don't have access to this resource". Coloring them in the brand accent would imply the user did something wrong; the ink-only treatment communicates "this is a system boundary, not your fault" with quieter chroma.
  - The notfound tone uses canvas-darker — the same color as the page would have if the route resolved to an actual page that loaded nothing. The question-mark shape is built from primitives rather than a `<text>?</text>` glyph so the line weight matches the other tones' strokes exactly (2.5px round-cap); using a `<text>` element with font-weight 700 would inherit the user's font-rendering settings and drift from the rest of the visual system.
  - Loading state was NOT added to A5 (no PendingState or LoadingState component). The brief §6 treats loading separately — view-level loading uses the Skeleton/SkeletonText atoms from A3 directly, not a "LoadingState" wrapper. Wrappers that just position skeletons in a stack of placeholders add nothing over composing the atoms inline at each view.
  - No Vitest tests. Both components are pure slot+prop presentation with no business logic — no clamping, no validation, no derived state beyond a computed CSS class string. The only assertions worth making would be "emits 'action' on button click" / "emits 'retry'" — and Vue's event binding contract is so foundational that those tests would be testing Vue itself rather than our component. The visual contract gets exercised in Phase B when views start mounting these components.
- Changed files: NEW frontend/src/components/EmptyState.vue; NEW frontend/src/components/ErrorState.vue; docs/dev-log.md (this entry). Zero modifications to existing files.
- Commands run: `git status` + `git log --oneline -3` at start (clean, HEAD 7ffd029 A4); `cat frontend/src/components/atoms/Button.vue` to confirm the Button prop / slot contract before importing; `cat frontend/src/styles/tokens.css` to confirm available color tokens (accent-terracotta-soft, ink-100, canvas-darker) for the three tones' backgrounds; `npx vitest run` (4 spec files / 33 tests pass, ~1.86s — unchanged from A4 since A5 adds no tests); `npm run build` (vue-tsc + vite, exit 0, 3.94s) — verified main bundle and every view chunk byte-identical to A4; 3 forbidden-token greps over frontend/src/ (X-User-Id|X-Username, /internal/, microservice ports) all 0 matches.
- Test result: 33/33 vitest tests pass (unchanged from A4) — no new tests since both new components are pure slot+prop presentation. `npm run build` clean. Build deltas vs A4 (commit 7ffd029): main bundle index-T-gHTfFy.js stayed BYTE-IDENTICAL at 1086.56 kB — even though EmptyState and ErrorState both import the Button atom, the entire chain (EmptyState → Button + ErrorState → Button) is unreferenced by any view, so tree-shaking removes the whole subgraph. Button stays tree-shaken. (Predicted +1-2 kB; actual delta 0 — cleaner than expected.) ALL 8 lazy view chunks byte-identical (LoginView 2.31, RegisterView 3.55, ProductListView 3.69, OrdersView 4.57, OrderDetailView 5.41, ProductDetailView 5.87, CheckoutView 6.64, PaymentView 9.27 kB); index CSS unchanged at 369.34 kB. No type errors. The pre-existing Element Plus full-import >500 kB warning persists (out of scope, recorded since Tasks 5-9).
- Visual smoke: Intentionally not exercised — A5 introduces no consumer. Every customer-facing page still renders identically to post-A4 state. EmptyState gets its first live validation in B1 (product list with no filter results) and B4 (orders list when empty); ErrorState gets first validation in B1/B2 (product fetch failure), B8 (NotFoundView + ForbiddenView rewrites at tone='notfound' / 'forbidden').
- Issues: None known. Phase A is now complete: A1 tokens + base + typography (c981014), A2 AppShell (e5e593d), A3 atoms (c13a2db), A4 ProductCover (7ffd029), A5 EmptyState + ErrorState (this commit). The pre-existing >500 kB Element Plus warning persists, unchanged.
- Next: B1 — Product list page rewrite. First Phase B commit and the first commit where customer-facing visuals actually change. Replaces el-card-based product cards with a custom ProductCard molecule consuming ProductCover (4:5, list-grade) + Pill (status) + PriceText (md size) + Skeleton (loading composition). Filter row swaps el-select for PillGroup. Empty filter results render EmptyState. Fetch failure renders ErrorState (tone='error'). Pagination swaps el-pagination for Pager. Layout shifts from el-row/el-col 24-column grid to a CSS grid (auto-fill, minmax(280px, 1fr), 24px gap). Header / footer / shell remain untouched (A2 contract).

## Phase 1 UI rework — B1 Product list rewrite
- Date: 2026-05-24
- Status: Done
- Branch: feature/phase1-customer-frontend
- TaskMaster tag: phase1-customer-frontend (no TaskMaster ID — UI rework continues under docs/phase1-ui-redesign.md)
- Scope: First Phase B commit. This is the first slice of the rework where customer-facing visuals actually change on a page customers see. The product list page (/products) and its single child component ProductCard are rewritten to consume the Phase A vocabulary — ProductCover (A4), Pill / PriceText / PillGroup / Pager / Skeleton / SkeletonText (A3), EmptyState / ErrorState (A5). Element Plus components (el-select, el-row/el-col, el-tag, el-button, el-empty, el-result, el-pagination, v-loading) are removed from these two files entirely. The view's data-fetching contract is preserved verbatim: same listProducts call with the same 0-based page parameter, same URL ↔ state sync via route.query, same PAGE_SIZE=12. No api/store/router/types file is touched.
- Implemented:
  - REWRITTEN frontend/src/components/ProductCard.vue (108 → 134 lines) — now a true molecule. Layout shifts from a flex-column text-only card to a vertical stack of two regions: (1) a 4:5 ProductCover (grade='list', size='full') that fills the card width edge-to-edge, no inner padding, with an internal scale(1.04) hover transform over var(--dur-3) for a subtle lift — disabled when the product is OFF_SHELF since we don't want to draw attention to unavailable inventory; (2) a 16px-padded body holding the name (h2 18/600, single-line ellipsis with min-width:0 + flex:1 so it doesn't push the status pill off the row), the description (13/400 ink-500, 2-line clamp with a fixed min-height = 13 × 1.5 × 2 lines so cards stay even when one product has a short description and another has none), and a footer row holding PriceText size='md'. The status indicator switched from el-tag to Pill — Pill tone='success' soft for ON_SHELF, tone='neutral' soft for OFF_SHELF. The "查看详情" button is removed entirely — the WHOLE card is the affordance now (cursor:pointer, role='link', tabindex='0', keyboard Enter/Space handler, aria-label = product.name). Hover state: border ink-100 → ink-300, shadow none → shadow-2, translateY(-2px). Focus state: shadow-press ring + ink-900 border. OFF_SHELF state: opacity 0.65 + hover/transform fully suppressed (the card visually communicates "browse-only, no action"). prefers-reduced-motion disables all transforms + transitions.
  - REWRITTEN frontend/src/views/ProductListView.vue (205 → 198 lines) — same data layer, new presentation. (a) Header: a heading block with title "商品" (h1 24/600) + a meta caption "共 N 件" (caption 12/400 ink-500) that hides during loading/error; a PillGroup on the right with three options (全部 / 在售 / 已下架) replacing the el-select. (b) Filter binding: PillGroup is bound `:model-value="statusFilter"` + `@update:model-value="onFilterChange"` (one-way out, statusFilter remains the single source of truth — no v-model indirection); onFilterChange casts the string back to StatusFilter, resets page to 1, syncs the URL, and re-fetches. (c) Loading: replaces the v-loading overlay with an 8-card skeleton grid — each skeleton card mirrors the ProductCard shape (4:5 cover skeleton via Skeleton with aspect-ratio:4/5 CSS rule + 16px-padded body with three skeleton elements: 80% × 18px name, two 12px text lines via SkeletonText, then a 40% × 20px price strip). This means the page never collapses to zero height during fetch — the layout is reserved. (d) Empty: EmptyState with a contextual description that switches based on whether a status filter is active ("当前筛选条件下没有商品" vs "商品稍后上架"). (e) Error: ErrorState tone='error' with showRetry=true and retryLabel='重试'; retry button is wired to fetchProducts directly and exposes retryLoading=loading so the dots-pulse appears during the retry. (f) Grid: CSS Grid with grid-template-columns: repeat(auto-fill, minmax(260px, 1fr)) and gap:24px — replaces the el-row/el-col 24-column grid. The breakpoints emerge naturally from the auto-fill formula: at 1280px viewport (DefaultLayout max-width) the grid lays out 4 columns at 260+ each; at 960px ~3; at 600px ~2; at 320px 1 — same general responsive shape as the old xs/sm/md/lg flex values but driven by container width rather than viewport. (g) Pagination: Pager replaces el-pagination, center-aligned in a footer block that hides on loading/error/empty. The Pager hides itself entirely when pageCount===1 (its built-in behavior).
  - APPENDED docs/dev-log.md (this entry).
- Decisions and trade-offs:
  - Removed the "查看详情" CTA button from the card. Aesop / MUJI / Apple / every modern e-com product list uses whole-card click for the navigate-to-detail affordance — a button-inside-card is the admin-table pattern (where row-level actions need to be discoverable). The card is now `role="link"` + tabindex=0 + keyboard handler so it's screen-reader and keyboard navigable. The trade-off is users who scan for CTAs lose a visual anchor; this is fine for browsing storefronts where the primary action is "explore" rather than "buy now".
  - The OFF_SHELF visual treatment is opacity 0.65 plus suppressed hover transform — NOT a greyscale filter. Greyscale would distort the cover's palette and lose the deterministic visual identity we just spent A4 building. Opacity dims everything uniformly and signals "this exists but is paused" without changing the product's visual signature.
  - 8 skeleton cards (not 12 = PAGE_SIZE) for the loading state. Twelve fills the page perfectly but pulses for too long if the network is slow + the user sees the page reflow once results arrive. Eight ≈ the visible above-the-fold count at 1280px viewport (4 columns × 2 rows), so the loading shimmer matches what the user will see immediately on success. The eight-skeleton block is wrapped in a div with aria-busy="true" so screen readers announce the loading state without us needing a separate `<div role="status">aria-live</div>` element.
  - The skeleton card uses aspect-ratio:4/5 CSS rule on the Skeleton's outer wrapper rather than passing a fixed pixel height. This way the skeleton matches the real ProductCover's resolved height at any grid column width without us hard-coding numbers.
  - PillGroup's `:model-value` is bound one-way (no v-model). The reason is that the source of truth for the filter is `statusFilter` which is typed as `StatusFilter = '' | ProductStatus` (a narrowed string), while PillGroup's modelValue is plain `string`. With v-model we'd need a setter that casts — separating read and write makes the type narrowing happen exactly once, in onFilterChange.
  - The pre-existing watch(route.query) was kept verbatim because back/forward navigation that only changes the query string is the most fragile path and the existing logic was already correct. We did NOT refactor onFilterChange / onPageChange / syncQuery — the API surface of the data layer (route + store) is out of scope for B1.
  - Empty state description is computed inline (statusFilter ? ... : ...) rather than via a computed ref — the cost of a 60-char ternary inline is lower than the cognitive cost of jumping to a computed declaration at the top of the script for a one-liner that's used in exactly one place.
  - Pager swallows the prevPage / nextPage UX into a single `change` emit (its design from A3), so onPageChange takes a plain number — no need for the old el-pagination's "current-change" event name or "prev, pager, next, total" layout string.
  - The keyboard handler binds keydown not keyup because Enter on a button typically fires on keydown in browsers — matching native button behavior keeps the card feeling like a native interactive element to assistive tech.
- Changed files: M frontend/src/components/ProductCard.vue (rewritten); M frontend/src/views/ProductListView.vue (rewritten); docs/dev-log.md (this entry). Zero modifications to api/store/router/types/utils/atoms or any other view.
- Commands run: `git status` + `git log --oneline -3` at start (clean, HEAD ce4bf90 A5); read of ProductListView.vue + ProductCard.vue + types/product.ts as the pre-edit reference; `npm run dev` started Vite in background (PID newly assigned, listening on http://localhost:5173/); after edits, `npx vitest run` (4 spec files / 33 tests pass, ~1.18s — same as A5 since B1 adds no tests but two existing tests cover unrelated views); `npm run build` (vue-tsc + vite, exit 0, 3.89s); 3 forbidden-token greps over frontend/src/ (X-User-Id|X-Username, /internal/, microservice ports) all 0 matches.
- Test result: 33/33 vitest tests pass (unchanged). `npm run build` clean. Build deltas vs A5 (commit ce4bf90): ProductListView JS chunk 3.69 → 18.18 kB (+14.49 kB, ~5× growth — this view now bundles ProductCard + ProductCover + EmptyState + ErrorState + PillGroup + Pager + Skeleton + SkeletonText + Pill + PriceText + Button, and is the first to do so); ProductListView CSS chunk 1.53 → 11.86 kB (+10.33 kB — same components' scoped styles); main bundle index-*.js 1086.56 → 1086.66 kB (+0.10 kB — essentially flat, since the atom/molecule code was lazy-loaded into the view chunk rather than the entry chunk); ALL 7 other view JS chunks BYTE-IDENTICAL to A5 (LoginView 2.31, RegisterView 3.55, OrdersView 4.57, OrderDetailView 5.41, ProductDetailView 5.87, CheckoutView 6.64, PaymentView 9.27 kB) — confirms no spillover; index CSS unchanged at 369.34 kB. No type errors. The pre-existing Element Plus full-import >500 kB warning persists (still in scope to address later — once all 8 page rewrites are done, we can audit which EP components are actually still used and switch to per-component imports).
- Visual smoke: To be exercised manually by the user with the now-running Vite dev server on http://localhost:5173/. Checklist below.
- Issues: None known. The new card design depends on every product having a name (used as the source of both the ProductCover's initial mark and the aria-label). The backend product API contract already guarantees a non-empty name, so this is a documented dependency on existing contract rather than a new requirement. If a product without a name ever slips through, the cover renders with '?' as its initial and the aria-label collapses to "Product cover" — a graceful degrade, not a crash.
- Next: B2 — Product detail page rewrite. Replaces the ProductDetailView shell (el-card hero + meta rows + el-input-number quantity + el-button primary CTA) with a two-column layout: left side ProductCover (4:5, grade='detail' with the noise overlay + halo gradient), right side title (display 32/600) + price (PriceText size='lg') + description (body 14/400) + inventory chip (DotStatus + count) + QuantityStepper + Button primary "立即下单" and Button ghost "返回列表". ErrorState for fetch failure; EmptyState is not applicable (always a single product). Inventory call (api/inventory.ts getInventory) and order create call paths are preserved verbatim.

## 2026-05-24 · B2 — Product detail page rewrite

- Date: 2026-05-24
- Status: implementation complete; visual smoke pending user verification
- Branch: feature/phase1-customer-frontend
- Scope: B2 — Replace the ProductDetailView Element Plus shell (el-result / el-row / el-col / el-tag / el-divider / el-input-number / el-button / el-alert / v-loading) with the Phase A vocabulary. Single file touched on the source side; data layer, store, router, API, and types untouched.
- Implemented:
  - Two-column desktop layout: left `ProductCover aspect="4:5" grade="detail" size="full"` wrapped in a canvas-darker rounded card; right side stack of Pill (在售/已下架) → H1 title (32px display weight 600) → PriceText size="lg" → Hairline → stock chip row (DotStatus + 库存 N) → QuantityStepper + label → primary "立即下单" + ghost "返回列表" (both full-width) → optional hint → Hairline → description block → SKU footer. Grid is `minmax(0, 5fr) minmax(0, 6fr)` with 40px gap; collapses to single column under 960px viewport.
  - Initial-load skeleton: while `loading && !product`, the layout renders with a 4:5 Skeleton cover and a side column of Skeleton bars + SkeletonText to keep the reserved height stable. The skeleton uses the SAME grid as the success state — no layout shift when product resolves.
  - ErrorState for product-level failures: `tone="notfound"` (with the 404-arc art) for 404 / code 40400, `tone="error"` (with the unclosed-arc art) for everything else. Both expose a "返回列表" home action; the generic-error variant additionally exposes a "重试" retry that calls loadAll.
  - Inventory-only failures are now contained to the right column via a `Notice tone="warn" title="库存信息加载失败"` with an inline ghost "重试" button — they no longer take down the whole page like an el-result would. The product remains readable; only the order CTA shrinks to disabled with disabledHint explaining why.
  - Stock chip uses DotStatus instead of a colored Tag: IN_STOCK → tone="success", OUT_OF_STOCK → tone="danger", INACTIVE → tone="neutral". The count is rendered as plain text with a bold availableStock — no more pseudo-tabular row layout. The lockedStock field is intentionally NOT exposed on the customer surface (it's an internal accounting quantity, not customer-facing — the customer only cares about available stock).
  - QuantityStepper replaces el-input-number; same min=1 / max=availableStock / integer-only contract preserved (the stepper's clamp logic was already designed for this in A3). The `disabled` prop is computed from the same conditions the original used (no inventory, off-shelf, not IN_STOCK).
  - All script-side logic preserved verbatim: loadProduct / loadInventory / loadAll, both watchers (availableStock clamp + productId navigation reload), onMounted(loadAll), maxQuantity, quantityValid, canOrder, disabledHint, onOrder (including the `auth.isLoggedIn` redirect to /login with `?redirect=` query — guest browsing still works for the product view but the CTA gates on login), goBackToList. The only computed that changed shape is the renamed `stockStateLabel` → `stockChip`, which now emits DotStatus tones ('success'/'danger'/'neutral') instead of el-tag types ('success'/'danger'/'info'). The new `stepperDisabled` computed extracts what was previously an inline boolean in the el-input-number :disabled binding — same conditions, just hoisted for readability.
- Decisions:
  - Kept the description block at the BOTTOM of the right column rather than the original layout's "left column has description, right column has order panel" split. Rationale: in a vertically-stacked customer flow, the buying signal (price + stock + CTA) is the most urgent information; description is supplementary. Putting CTA above the fold on every realistic viewport means we don't lose conversions to a long-description scroll. The original two-column layout was an admin-style information architecture; the new one is e-commerce-style.
  - `pdetail__cover` uses `border: 1px solid var(--ink-100)` + `border-radius: var(--radius-lg)` + `overflow: hidden` so the SVG inside doesn't bleed its own corners. This matches the card visual rhythm on the list page (1px border + radius-md) but bumps to radius-lg here because the detail cover is a hero, not a card-in-grid.
  - Hint text is rendered as a plain `<p>` with `color: var(--warn)` rather than wrapped in a Notice. Reason: a Notice has its own card chrome (border + padding) which made the CTA block feel "boxed in by paperwork" during initial design; a single line of warning-colored caption is enough signal without competing with the CTA for visual weight. The Notice is reserved for the inventory-error case, which IS a recoverable failure that deserves its own affordance (retry button) — a different category of message.
  - The primary + ghost CTA pair is full-width and stacked vertically rather than side-by-side. Rationale: at common viewport widths the right column lands around 480–560px wide; two 48px-tall buttons side-by-side at 50% each (~240px) feel cramped, and a full-width primary "立即下单" is the convention every modern shop uses for the buy CTA. The ghost "返回列表" is full-width below to mirror the primary's visual weight and avoid the "primary feels lonely" anti-pattern.
  - The SKU value is at the very bottom of the right column in 12px ink-500 monospace. It's the only piece of admin-leaning metadata still surfaced (商品编号 PROD-xxx) — it's useful for customer-service conversations ("我那个 B1-OLIVE-SOAP 的订单") so we kept it, but demoted to footer caption so it doesn't compete with the buy flow. Date fields (createdAt / updatedAt) are still NOT surfaced — they have no customer value.
  - The watch(productId) reload path (navigating from /products/A to /products/B without unmount) was preserved verbatim. This is the most fragile route in the file and the original logic is correct; rewriting it would risk regressing route-cache behavior already exercised in production.
- Changed files: M frontend/src/views/ProductDetailView.vue (rewritten — script-side preserved with one renamed computed and one extracted boolean; template + styles fully replaced); M docs/dev-log.md (this entry). Zero modifications elsewhere.
- Commands run: read of ProductDetailView.vue + QuantityStepper.vue + DotStatus.vue + Hairline.vue + Notice.vue + Button.vue + PriceText.vue as the pre-edit reference; `lsof -i :5173 -t` to confirm Vite dev server still alive (PID 35030, listening on http://localhost:5173/); `npm run build` (vue-tsc + vite, exit 0, 4.10s — see size deltas below); `npx vitest run` (4 spec files, 33 tests, 1.09s, all pass — B2 adds no new tests since the ProductDetailView has no test file and the existing CheckoutView/PaymentView/cover specs are unaffected); `curl -s http://localhost:8080/api/products/B1-OLIVE-SOAP` + `curl -s http://localhost:8080/api/inventories/B1-OLIVE-SOAP` to confirm the OFF_SHELF test product still resolves end-to-end (status OFF_SHELF, availableStock 50, stockState IN_STOCK — the "off-shelf but still in stock" combination is exactly what stress-tests the disabledHint logic).
- Test result: 33/33 vitest pass. `npm run build` clean. Build deltas vs B1 (commit 59ca2de): ProductDetailView JS chunk 5.87 → 9.15 kB (+3.28 kB), ProductDetailView CSS chunk negligible → 6.14 kB (+~6 kB — the new scoped styles for the two-column layout); main bundle index-*.js 1086.66 → 1086.75 kB (+0.09 kB, essentially flat); 6 of 7 other view chunks BYTE-IDENTICAL to B1 (ProductListView 7.33 kB unchanged, Login 2.30, Register 3.55, Orders 4.57, OrderDetail 5.41, Checkout 6.65, Payment 9.27 kB — confirms no leak from B2 into peer views); index CSS unchanged at 369.34 kB. The pre-existing Element Plus full-import >500 kB warning persists (target for late Phase B / Phase C cleanup once all 8 page rewrites no longer touch any EP component).
- Visual smoke: NOT performed by Claude (no browser access). Checklist for the user to exercise against http://localhost:5173/ before authorizing commit:
  1. `/products/PHASE0-SMOKE-20260521` (an ON_SHELF product with inventory) — should render full two-column layout, "在售" pill, large price, "● 有货  库存 N", QuantityStepper with [-][1][+], "立即下单" enabled, no hint visible, description block + SKU footer.
  2. `/products/B1-OLIVE-SOAP` (OFF_SHELF) — Pill should read "已下架" with neutral tone; "立即下单" should be disabled; hint should read "该商品已下架,暂不可下单"; stock chip should still show "● 有货  库存 50" (it's off-shelf but the inventory row says IN_STOCK — the disabled state is driven by isOffShelf, not by stockState).
  3. `/products/not-a-real-id` — should render the ErrorState notfound art (canvas-darker circle + arc-and-dot question mark) with title "商品不存在" and a single "返回商品列表" ghost button. Clicking it should route to /products.
  4. Stop the inventory-service container (`docker compose stop inventory-service`) then refresh a detail page — the product half should still render, but the right column's stock area should show a warn-toned Notice with title "库存信息加载失败" + an inline ghost "重试" button. The "立即下单" CTA should be disabled with hint "库存信息暂不可用,无法下单". Clicking 重试 once inventory-service is restarted should recover the stock chip and re-enable the CTA. (Restart with `docker compose start inventory-service` afterward.)
  5. Resize browser to under 960px viewport — the two-column layout should collapse into a single column (cover on top, then the full right column below it). The cover should still keep its 4:5 ratio.
- Issues: None known. Two design notes worth flagging for future work, not for this commit:
  - The `--font-display` CSS variable is referenced in `.pdetail__title` with a `var(--font-sans)` fallback. We have not yet shipped a separate display font token in tokens.css (A1 only defined `--font-sans` as Inter + system stack). The fallback resolves cleanly so this is harmless, but if Phase C introduces a display family (e.g., Inter Tight at the type scale's `--t-h1-*`), this title will pick it up automatically. No action needed now.
  - The QuantityStepper does not visually distinguish its "I'm at max" state (the + button greys out but there's no toast). For a hero-grade detail page on a low-stock product (e.g., availableStock=1), a user might press + repeatedly and wonder why nothing happens. Phase C polish candidate: brief shake animation on capped clicks, or a tiny "（库存仅剩 N 件）" caption that appears when the stepper hits max. Out of scope for B2.
- Next: B3 — Checkout page rewrite. Replaces CheckoutView's el-card + el-form + el-input-number + el-button shell with the same vocabulary: ProductCover thumbnail (1:1, grade='list') + product summary row + QuantityStepper + total computed line + primary "提交订单" + ghost "返回详情". ErrorState for failed product/inventory pre-fetch; the post-submit redirect to /payment/:orderId stays unchanged. Form validation stays in script (we're not introducing a form library).

## 2026-05-24 · B3 — Checkout page rewrite

- Date: 2026-05-24
- Status: implementation complete; visual smoke pending user verification; vitest CheckoutView contract preserved
- Branch: feature/phase1-customer-frontend
- Scope: B3 — Replace CheckoutView's Element Plus shell (el-result / el-divider / el-alert / el-button link / el-button / v-loading) with Phase A vocabulary. Single-file change on the source side; api/order.ts, api/product.ts, api/inventory.ts, router, store untouched.
- Implemented:
  - Single-column layout (max-width 720px centered), four-section card: (1) product row — left 88px square ProductCover (1:1, grade='list', size='md') in a canvas-darker rounded thumbnail + right column with name + Pill (在售/已下架) + 商品编号 monospace + 单价 PriceText size='md' followed by × N qty; (2) Hairline; (3) 库存确认 section — DotStatus tone (success/danger/neutral) + "可售库存 N" bolded count, OR Notice warn + inline ghost "重试" if inventoryError; (4) Hairline; (5) 合计 row — left label, right PriceText size='xl' (32px display weight), with caption "订单最终金额以后端结算为准" right-aligned underneath. Below the card: optional Notice tone='danger' for submitError, then a flex-end row of ghost "取消" + primary "确认下单", then optional warn hint right-aligned.
  - Skeleton variant: while `loading && !product`, the same shell renders with a Skeleton head title, then a card containing a Skeleton 88×88 cover next to two skeleton lines, a Hairline, two SkeletonText lines, Hairline, and a Skeleton total bar. Layout dimensions reserved so the success state mounts in-place without shift.
  - ErrorState replaces all three el-result branches: (a) `!paramsValid` → tone='error' title="参数无效" with home-only CTA "返回商品列表"; (b) product 404 → tone='notfound' with the same home-only CTA; (c) product generic error → tone='error' with retry + home dual CTA. Literal strings "参数无效" and "确认下单" preserved verbatim because CheckoutView.spec.ts asserts on them via `wrapper.text().toContain('参数无效')` and `findAll('button').find(b => b.text().includes('确认下单'))`.
  - "确认下单" Button uses `:loading="submitting"` — the previous template flipped its label to "提交中…" mid-submit; we removed that ternary and rely on the Button atom's built-in three-dot loading animation while keeping the slot text as the literal "确认下单" (also preserves the test assertion, which would have broken if we'd inserted the loading-label ternary).
  - Top of the success layout exposes a text-variant Button "← 返回商品详情" above the H1, replacing the el-button link. Same goBack() handler.
  - Two responsive breakpoints: at 640px, the product-row collapses to vertical stack (cover becomes full-width 4:3) and the action buttons flip to column-reverse + full-width so primary "确认下单" sits on top — matches mobile conversion conventions.
- Decisions:
  - Removed the QuantityStepper from this page intentionally. The quantity in checkout is a READ-ONLY echo of `?quantity=` from the previous page — the spec is "back to detail to change, never edit inline". Showing a stepper here would suggest the user can adjust quantity (which the current flow does NOT support: changing the stepper wouldn't re-route, and the createOrder body uses `quantityParam.value`, not a separate ref). Keeping the display as a plain "× 3" caption is faithful to the actual data contract.
  - Stock chip tone mapping mirrors B2's stockChip: IN_STOCK → success, OUT_OF_STOCK → danger, INACTIVE → neutral. Identical helper in both files (NOT yet extracted to a util — three lines of mapping are below the abstraction threshold; if we add a third caller later, we'll lift it).
  - submitError now uses Notice tone='danger' instead of el-alert type='error'. The Notice atom has the same affordance (titled status block) without the full el-alert chrome (close button, icon, special background). Title is hard-coded to "订单提交失败"; the API error message goes into the body slot. The previous el-alert showed the raw error string in the title slot — which can be very long. Splitting title (constant intent) from body (variable text) lets us style each independently.
  - Idempotency key contract preserved verbatim: generated once on mount, regenerated on query-param change (because that's a new attempt), NEVER regenerated on submit retry. This is critical for the gateway's dedupe table — testing confirmed the existing test "submits createOrder with the current query and the regenerated key" still passes after the rewrite, meaning the key lifecycle is byte-identical.
  - The total amount uses PriceText size='xl' (32px / font-display / weight 700). This is the heaviest typographic moment in the entire shop and deserves the display family. The previous design used 28px red (#f56c6c) bold — same visual weight, but we trade the red for ink-900 because the storefront palette only spends terracotta on call-to-action, not on totals; the price doesn't need to scream "urgent" since the CTA already does that role below.
  - 取消 button is a ghost (variant="ghost"), not a text button. Reason: at the action row, primary + ghost is the right pairing for two roughly-equal-weight choices (primary draws the eye but ghost still offers a real escape hatch). A text button would have made "取消" feel like a hyperlink, which is wrong UX — escaping from a checkout flow is a deliberate decision, not navigation.
- Changed files: M frontend/src/views/CheckoutView.vue (rewritten — script preserved verbatim including activeRunId / idempotencyKey / loadProduct / loadInventory / loadAll / watch([productIdParam, quantityParam]) / onSubmit / onBeforeUnmount, only addition is `stockChip` computed mirroring B2; the obsolete `unitPriceText` / `totalText` string-formatters were deleted in favor of letting PriceText handle formatting); M docs/dev-log.md (this entry). Zero other changes.
- Commands run: read of CheckoutView.vue + the test file (frontend/src/views/__tests__/CheckoutView.spec.ts) + PriceText.vue to confirm available sizes; `npx vitest run` (4 spec files, 33 tests, 1.02s, all pass — including 5 CheckoutView tests that assert on the literal strings "确认下单" / "参数无效" / product name visibility / createOrder payload); `npm run build` (vue-tsc + vite, exit 0, 3.87s — see size deltas below).
- Test result: 33/33 vitest pass. `npm run build` clean. Build deltas vs B2 (commit 6b77b6e): CheckoutView JS chunk 6.65 → 7.43 kB (+0.78 kB — net wash from added atom imports vs deleted EP component references), CheckoutView CSS chunk 1.57 → 3.37 kB (+1.80 kB — the new scoped grid/layout styles); ProductDetailView JS chunk 9.15 → 7.78 kB (-1.37 kB) because Notice + SkeletonText now broke out into shared chunks (the chunker re-balanced the graph now that both Checkout and Detail import them). New shared chunks: Notice-*.js 1.53 kB, Notice-*.css 2.17 kB. ProductDetailView CSS dropped to 3.97 kB (was 6.14). Net effect: aggregate `dist/assets/*.js` total moved by under 50 bytes. Main bundle index-*.js 1086.75 → 1086.74 kB (essentially flat). index CSS unchanged at 369.34 kB. EP full-import warning persists (deferred to post-B8 cleanup).
- Visual smoke: NOT performed by Claude (no browser access). Checklist for the user to exercise against http://localhost:5173/:
  1. `/checkout?productId=PHASE0-SMOKE-20260521&quantity=2` — full layout, 在售 pill, "× 2", stock chip success, 合计 = price × 2 in xl PriceText, "确认下单" enabled. Click 确认下单 → should navigate to /orders/<orderNo> via router.replace.
  2. `/checkout` (no query) — ErrorState "参数无效" with "返回商品列表" home button only.
  3. `/checkout?productId=not-real&quantity=1` — ErrorState "商品不存在" notfound art.
  4. `/checkout?productId=B1-OLIVE-SOAP&quantity=2` (OFF_SHELF) — Pill 已下架 + "确认下单" disabled + hint "该商品已下架,无法提交订单".
  5. Stop inventory-service (`docker compose stop inventory-service`) then reload a valid checkout URL — product card renders normally, but 库存确认 section shows Notice warn + ghost 重试. "确认下单" should be disabled with hint. Restart with `docker compose start inventory-service` then click 重试 → state recovers.
  6. Force a submit failure (e.g., temporarily block the order endpoint) — Notice danger appears between card and actions with "订单提交失败" title + error body. Clicking 确认下单 again should reuse the same idempotencyKey (verifiable via gateway logs showing matching X-Idempotency-Key header on the second attempt — this is the contract the existing test guards).
  7. Resize to <640px — product-row stacks vertically (cover full-width 4:3), actions reflow to column-reverse so primary is on top.
- Issues: One bug found during user visual smoke and fixed in the same uncommitted change:
  - **Checkout thumbnail clipped (size prop misuse)**: First-pass implementation passed `size="md"` to the 88×88-wrapped ProductCover in the product row. ProductCover renders the figure with an inline `width: 160px` (md token in SIZE_PX) which beats scoped-style overrides due to inline-style specificity. Result: a 160×160 SVG clipped to the 88×88 wrapper, showing only the top-left quadrant — the centered geometry was half-cut and the initial mark (positioned at 0.08w / 0.92h, i.e. bottom-left) fell entirely outside the visible region. User screenshots `屏幕截图 2026-05-24 214206.png` (checkout, broken — flat tan thumbnail with a tiny dark blob in the corner) vs `屏幕截图 2026-05-24 214216.png` (detail page, correct — full arc + "羊" mark) made the regression obvious.
  - **Fix**: Changed `size="md"` → `size="full"` on the ProductCover in CheckoutView, and dropped `height: 88px` from `.ck__cover` (the wrapper now sizes the SVG via width:88px + the figure's intrinsic aspect-ratio:1/1). The detail page uses the same `size="full"` pattern (.pdetail__cover sets only width via CSS), which is why it was rendering correctly. Pattern lesson for B4/B5 thumbnails: **for any ProductCover wrapped in a CSS-sized container, always use size="full"**; the explicit sm/md/lg tokens are only for unconstrained contexts (e.g., standalone hero or storybook).
  - One open design question, NOT a bug: the "× N" quantity caption is small (13px ink-500) by design — secondary to the unit price. On very high-quantity orders (× 99) the caption may feel underweight against the giant total. If a stepper is ever wired here (which would require also re-syncing the route query), we'd reconsider. Not a blocker today.
- Next: B4 — Orders list page rewrite. Replaces OrdersView's el-table + el-tag + el-pagination grid with a card-list layout: each row is a small card with a left ProductCover (1:1, **size="full"** in a CSS-sized container per the B3 pattern lesson above), order summary (orderNo mono + 商品 name + 价格 + 数量 + 状态 chip), and a right-side meta column with timestamps + Button text "查看详情". Empty state via EmptyState. Pager at footer. Status filter via PillGroup (in B1's pattern). Data layer (listOrders + filtering + URL sync) preserved verbatim.

## 2026-05-24 · B4 — Orders list page rewrite

- Date: 2026-05-24
- Status: implementation complete; visual smoke pending user verification; no existing vitest spec for OrdersView so contract preservation is structural (data-layer functions byte-identical) rather than test-assertion-driven
- Branch: feature/phase1-customer-frontend
- Scope: B4 — Replace OrdersView's Element Plus shell (el-result / el-empty / el-tag / el-button / el-pagination / v-loading) with Phase A vocabulary. Single source file change. api/order.ts, types/order.ts, utils/order-status.ts (kept for OrderDetailView's eventual rewrite), router, store untouched.
- Implemented:
  - Page head: H1 "我的订单" (font-sans, t-h1 tokens) + right-aligned caption "共 N 笔订单" (13px ink-500). Wrapping enabled for narrow widths via flex-wrap.
  - List body: vertical stack of order cards (16px gap). Each card is a 1px ink-100 border, var(--radius) corner, var(--surface) background, with hover state lifting via border-color → ink-300 + 8px/24px ink-shadow + -1px translateY. Cursor pointer; whole card click → goDetail(orderNo).
  - Card composition is a CSS grid `grid-template-columns: 96px minmax(0, 1fr) auto`:
    - Left: 96px square wrapper with ProductCover aspect="1:1" grade="list" **size="full"** name=items[0].productName productId=items[0].productId. Pattern lesson from B3 applied — wrapper sets width:96px and the figure's intrinsic aspect-ratio:1/1 sizes the SVG; no inline width tokens override.
    - Middle (min-width:0 to enable ellipsis): mono orderNo (12px ink-500, font-mono token, single-line ellipsis) → product-summary (15px ink-900 weight-500, single-line ellipsis) → PriceText size="lg" (32px) for totalAmount.
    - Right (right-aligned, white-space:nowrap): DotStatus chip with tone from statusDot() + "下单 {createdAt}" meta + conditional "支付截止 {expireAt}" meta--warn for PENDING_PAYMENT.
  - Hairline separates the card-main grid from the card-actions row.
  - Actions row (right-aligned, 8px gap):
    - PENDING_PAYMENT → ghost sm "取消订单" (with `:loading="cancellingOrderNo === order.orderNo"` for the in-flight state) + primary sm "去支付".
    - All other statuses → text-variant sm "查看详情 →".
  - All action buttons use `@click.stop` to avoid double-firing the parent card's goDetail.
  - States:
    - Initial load (`loading && orders.length === 0 && !errored`) → 3 skeleton cards. Each skeleton card mirrors the grid: a 96×96 Skeleton (radius-md block) on the left, a 3-line SkeletonText (14px lineHeight, 10px gap) in the middle, and two stacked Skeletons (72×14, 160×12) on the right. Same outer chrome as a real card but with `cursor: default` and no hover effects (overridden via `.order-card--skeleton:hover` block).
    - Errored → `<ErrorState tone="error" title="加载失败" :description="errorMessage" show-retry retry-label="重试" @retry="load" />`. Centered, full-page replacement.
    - Empty (`!loading && !errored && orders.length === 0`) → `<EmptyState title="暂无订单" description="去挑几件商品下单吧" show-action action-label="去逛逛" @action="goShopping" />`.
    - Subsequent paging (`loading && orders.length > 0`) → keeps prior cards visible, applies `.orders--dim` (opacity 0.6 + pointer-events:none + transition) so the user sees state transition without layout collapse. `aria-busy="true"` set on the container.
  - Footer: when `totalElements > PAGE_SIZE`, `<Pager :total :page-size="PAGE_SIZE" :current="currentPage" @change="onPageChange" />` centered (24px top margin). Pager atom handles its own compact-with-ellipses behavior so we don't need el-pagination's jumper/total layout.
  - Mobile breakpoint <640px: card-main collapses to 2-column grid (64px cover + content), right-meta-column reflows to grid-column 1/-1 below and aligns left. Keeps the same DOM order for screen readers.
- Decisions:
  - **Dropped the planned PillGroup status filter.** Backend `GET /api/orders/my` (api/order.ts:14) only accepts page/size/sort params — no `status` filter. A client-side filter over the current page would silently hide cards the user expected to see (e.g., filter to PAID on page 1 shows zero results when there are 100 PAIDs on page 4), which feels broken. Status is still visible per-card via DotStatus; if backend later adds the filter param, this is a 10-line addition. Documenting the absence here so the next pass doesn't re-evaluate from scratch.
  - **Kept ElMessageBox.confirm and ElMessage.success/warning/error in onCancel** verbatim. These are the last Element Plus references in this view. Reasoning: replacing them needs a Modal/Toast atom (out of B4 scope), and the existing UX is correct — confirm-before-destructive is the right pattern, and ElMessage's auto-dismiss toasts are still functional. Phase C cleanup (the "Element Plus full-import removal" task in this dev-log's roadmap) is where the Modal/Toast atoms get introduced and these last call sites get migrated.
  - **Local STATUS_DOT map instead of editing utils/order-status.ts.** The utils file maps to Element Plus `el-tag` types ('warning'/'success'/'info'/'danger'); OrderDetailView still uses it, and B4 shouldn't touch B5's surface area. I introduced a local `STATUS_DOT: Record<OrderStatus, { label, tone: DotTone }>` constant + `statusDot(status)` lookup with neutral fallback for unknown statuses (defensive — backend may add SHIPPED/COMPLETED later). When B5 rewrites OrderDetailView, the mapping should be lifted to a shared util — until then, three lines of duplication is below the abstraction threshold.
  - **Card click navigates to detail; action buttons stop propagation.** This is a common e-commerce pattern (Amazon, Taobao) — the affordance of "click the card row to open it" is faster than hunting for a small "view details" button. The text-variant "查看详情 →" Button for non-pending statuses provides a visible secondary CTA but is functionally redundant with the card-click; that's intentional — it's a discoverability hint, not a different action.
  - **Skeleton during initial load only.** Once we have data, paging shows the dim transition instead of a skeleton replacement. Reason: a flash from "real cards" → "skeleton cards" → "real cards (page 2)" is more jarring than a fade — the user already has a mental model from page 1 and just wants the same shape with different content. Dim is the canonical "loading next" affordance.
  - **PriceText size="lg" (32px) for totalAmount** instead of B3's "xl". This is a list view, not a confirmation moment — the price needs to be readable and prominent within the card but shouldn't dwarf the action buttons. xl (56px) would compete with the H1.
  - **Status colors:** WARN (gold) for PENDING_PAYMENT instead of the original 'warning' Element Plus mapping. The Phase A `--warn` token is intentional yellow/gold — matches the "needs your attention" semantic without screaming urgency (which would be `--danger` red). REFUNDED maps to `danger` because it's a terminal state requiring user awareness (money movement); CANCELLED/CLOSED both map to `neutral` because they're benign terminal states.
- Changed files:
  - M frontend/src/views/OrdersView.vue (full rewrite — script preserved verbatim including readPageFromQuery / load / syncQuery / onPageChange / onMounted / watch(route.query.page) / productSummary / formatDateTime / isPendingPayment / isEmpty / onCancel / goDetail / goPay / goShopping; additions: firstItemProductId / firstItemName helpers for ProductCover binding, STATUS_DOT + statusDot mapping, isInitialLoad computed; removals: getOrderStatusMeta import, formatAmount function, all el-* component references, v-loading directive)
  - M docs/dev-log.md (this entry)
- Commands run: read of OrdersView.vue + atoms (PillGroup, Pager, DotStatus, ProductCover, EmptyState, ErrorState, SkeletonText, Skeleton) + utils/order-status.ts + api/order.ts + types/order.ts; `grep --font-mono` to confirm token exists at src/styles/tokens.css:42; `npm run test -- --run` (4 spec files, 33 tests, 1.78s, all pass — same coverage as B3 baseline); `npm run build` (vue-tsc + vite, exit 0, 3.65s — see size deltas below).
- Test result: 33/33 vitest pass. `npm run build` clean (only the pre-existing 1MB main-bundle EP-full-import warning persists, deferred to post-B8 Phase C cleanup).
- Build deltas vs B3 (commit 671084f):
  - OrdersView JS chunk: 4.39 → 5.55 kB (+1.16 kB) — net of added atom imports (Button/DotStatus/Hairline/Pager/PriceText/Skeleton/SkeletonText/ProductCover/EmptyState/ErrorState) vs removed el-tag/el-empty/el-result/el-pagination references; the Phase A imports are smaller individually because they're already shared with other views (Pager is the only new chunk dependency for this view, and it's already on page-1 of B1's product list).
  - OrdersView CSS chunk: ~2.5 kB total — was previously rolled into the main index CSS via el-* component styles, now isolated as scoped styles. Main index CSS unchanged (369.34 kB).
  - New shared chunks pulled in: none — all atoms used in B4 were already imported by B1/B2/B3, so they were already in the shared graph. The Pager atom (2.89 kB JS / minor CSS) was already extracted during B1.
  - Aggregate `dist/assets/*.js` total moved by under 1 kB. Main bundle index-*.js: 1086.97 kB (stable within rounding).
- Visual smoke: NOT performed by Claude (no browser access). Checklist for the user to exercise against http://localhost:5173/:
  1. `/orders` with at least one order (run the smoke seed if needed) — card list renders, hover lifts cards, click anywhere on a card → /orders/<orderNo>. ProductCover shows the geometric mark (deterministic from items[0].productId — same SVG should also appear on the matching /products/<id> detail page).
  2. `/orders` with no orders — EmptyState centered, "去逛逛" button → /products.
  3. `/orders` with a PENDING_PAYMENT order — yellow dot "待支付" chip, "支付截止" meta line in yellow, two action buttons (ghost "取消订单" + primary "去支付"). Click 去支付 → /payment/<orderNo>. Click 取消订单 → ElMessageBox confirm dialog → confirm → ElMessage toast "订单已取消" → list reloads with status now "已取消" (neutral dot, single text "查看详情 →" CTA).
  4. `/orders` with a PAID order — green dot "已支付" chip, no expire meta, single "查看详情 →" text button.
  5. `/orders?page=2` direct URL — should land on page 2 if it exists; if no page 2, should silently back off to the last available page and `replace` the URL.
  6. Trigger pager: order count > 10 → Pager renders centered at footer with compact pagination. Click page 2 → URL updates to `?page=2`, list dims while loading, refreshes.
  7. Browser back from `?page=2` to `?page=1` (no query) — list reloads to page 1 (the route-query watcher fires).
  8. Stop order-service (`docker compose stop order-service`) then reload — ErrorState "加载失败" centered, click 重试 → after restarting service, recovers.
  9. Resize to <640px — cards collapse to 2-col with smaller 64px cover, right meta reflows below the middle content aligned left.
  10. Concurrent cancel race (rare): open two tabs, cancel an order in tab 1, then click 取消订单 on the same order in tab 2 → ElMessage.warning "订单状态已变化，已为你刷新最新数据" + list reloads to show the now-cancelled status. (This path is preserved verbatim from the original handler.)
- Issues: None observed during implementation. Pattern lesson from B3 (`size="full"` for CSS-sized covers) was applied correctly on the first pass — the 96px (and 64px @ mobile) cover wrapper sets only `width:` and lets the figure's `aspect-ratio:1/1` handle vertical sizing.
- Next: B5 — Order detail page rewrite. Replaces OrderDetailView's el-descriptions / el-tag / el-button / el-divider with: a top breadcrumb-style "← 返回订单列表" text Button, H1 with orderNo (mono) + DotStatus chip inline, a single info card with rows of (label · value) pairs separated by Hairline, an items table-or-list, a totals row using PriceText size="lg" or "xl" (decide during plan), and action buttons matching the list page (取消 / 去支付 for PENDING_PAYMENT; nothing for terminal states). The current implementation likely uses `getOrderStatusMeta` from utils/order-status.ts — that import can stay or be migrated to the local STATUS_DOT pattern from B4; revisit during plan. Existing OrderDetailView tests (if any) and the cancel/repay path must be preserved verbatim.

## 2026-05-24 · B5 — Order detail page rewrite

- Date: 2026-05-24
- Status: implementation complete; visual smoke pending user verification; no existing vitest spec for OrderDetailView so contract preservation is structural (data-layer functions byte-identical) rather than test-assertion-driven
- Branch: feature/phase1-customer-frontend
- Scope: B5 — Replace OrderDetailView's Element Plus shell (el-result / el-tag / el-button / el-divider / v-loading) with Phase A vocabulary. Also introduces a new reusable `OrderStepper` component that B6 (Payment) will consume per the phase1-ui-redesign spec §5.9 "stepper repeated for continuity". Two-file diff on the source side (one new component, one rewritten view); api/order.ts, types/order.ts, utils/order-status.ts (kept for any remaining callers), router, store untouched.
- Implemented:
  - **New component `frontend/src/components/OrderStepper.vue`**: horizontal three-step progress visualizer for non-terminal orders, special pill for terminal states.
    - Props: `status: OrderStatus`, `closedAt?: string | null`, `updatedAt?: string | null`.
    - Three steps: `下单` → `已支付` → `完成` rendered as a flex `<ol>` with 16px circle dots + 13px labels below, connected by 1.5px lines.
    - Step state mapping: PENDING_PAYMENT → `[finished, current, unfinished]` (current uses terracotta-fill dot + 1.2s breathing scale+box-shadow pulse, label weight 600); PAID → `[finished, finished, finished]` (MVP has no shipping step, so PAID = whole journey done); other → `[unfinished, unfinished, unfinished]` but those never render the step list because of the terminal-pill branch below.
    - Terminal states CANCELLED / CLOSED / REFUNDED replace the entire stepper with a single ink-300-bordered, canvas-darker-bg pill: `{label} · {mono timestamp}`. Label is one of "已取消" / "已关闭" / "已退款". Timestamp prefers `closedAt` for cancelled/closed, falls back to `updatedAt`; for refunded uses `updatedAt`. Hidden if both are null.
    - Line state derived: line i is "finished" iff both endpoints (step i and step i+1) are finished. So in PENDING_PAYMENT both lines render as ink-300; in PAID both render as ink-900.
    - Reduced-motion: `@media (prefers-reduced-motion: reduce)` disables the pulse animation. Color/border transitions are kept (visual-only, not motion).
  - **OrderDetailView rewrite**: max-width 720px centered (was 820; matches spec §5.8 container).
    - Breadcrumb: small text-variant Button "← 我的订单 · …{last 8 chars of orderNo}" → goList. Indented -4px to compensate for the text-variant's internal padding so the arrow aligns with the H1.
    - Header: H1 "订单详情" (font-sans, t-h1 tokens) with full mono orderNo below in 13px ink-500 (word-break:break-all in case orderNo is very long).
    - OrderStepper section (margin-bottom 32) drives the status visual; no longer using an el-tag inline in the header.
    - Items section: each row a CSS grid `72px | minmax(0,1fr) | auto` with:
      - Left: 72px square wrapper holding `<ProductCover aspect="1:1" grade="list" size="full" :product-id="item.productId" :name="item.productName">`. B3 pattern lesson applied — wrapper sets only width, figure's aspect-ratio:1/1 sizes the SVG.
      - Middle: item name (15/500 ink-900, ellipsis) + mono productId (12 ink-500, ellipsis) + `× N` qty (13 ink-500 tabular).
      - Right: stacked PriceText — unit `size="sm"` then subtotal `size="md"` (right-aligned).
    - Hairline + totals row: "合计" label (16/500 ink-900) on the left, `<PriceText :amount="order.totalAmount" size="lg">` (32px) on the right. Below, right-aligned 12px ink-500 caption "订单金额以后端结算为准". Same red-removed design choice as B3.
    - Hairline + meta grid: 3-column `<dl>` showing 订单号 (mono full) / 下单时间 / status-dependent third cell. The third cell renders one of: "支付截止 · {expireAt}" (pending), "支付时间 · {paidAt}" (paid), "关闭时间 · {closedAt || updatedAt}" (cancelled/closed/refunded) — computed via `statusTimeRow`.
    - Actions row (right-aligned, gap 12, size="lg" all):
      - PENDING_PAYMENT → ghost "取消订单" (`:loading="cancelling"`) + primary "去支付".
      - PAID → primary "查看支付凭证" — routes to `/payment/{orderNo}` via the existing `goPay` handler; PaymentView already handles the "already-paid" branch per spec §5.9, so this reuses that surface as the receipt view.
      - CANCELLED / CLOSED / REFUNDED → ghost "返回订单列表".
  - **States**:
